<section id="Ch1" class="ltx_chapter">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_chapter">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_chapter">Chapter 1 </span>Group Theory</h2>

<div id="Ch1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">First, we describe the application of groups in revealing structure in other mathematical objects.
Then, we study the relationship between groups, culminating in a classification of groups of order <math id="Ch1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="pq" display="inline"><mrow><mi>p</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>q</mi></mrow></math>, where <math id="Ch1.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p" display="inline"><mi>p</mi></math> and <math id="Ch1.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="q" display="inline"><mi>q</mi></math> are primes.</p>
</div>
<section id="Ch1.S1" class="ltx_section">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">1.1 </span>Groups and Actions</h3>

<section id="Ch1.S1.SS1" class="ltx_subsection">
<h4 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">1.1.1 </span>Beginnings</h4>

<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem1" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 1.1.1</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">A group <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(G,e,\cdot)" display="inline"><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>G</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>e</mi><mo rspace="0em">,</mo><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">⋅</mo><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></math> is a set with an associative binary operation, s.t.</span></p>
<ul id="Ch1.S1.I1" class="ltx_itemize">
<li id="Ch1.S1.I1.i1" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S1.I1.i1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.S1.I1.i1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\forall a,b,c\in G,a\cdot(b\cdot c)=(a\cdot b)\cdot c" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo rspace="0.167em">∀</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow><mo>,</mo><mi>b</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow><mo rspace="0.055em" stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"></span></p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="Ch1.S1.I1.i2" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S1.I1.i2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.S1.I1.i2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\forall g\in G,\exists g^{-1}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo rspace="0.167em">∀</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mi>G</mi><mo>,</mo><mrow><mo rspace="0.167em">∃</mo><msup><mi>g</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup></mrow></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> s.t. </span><math id="Ch1.S1.I1.i2.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="gg^{-1}=g^{-1}g=e" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msup><mi>g</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msup><mi>g</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup><mo>⁢</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>e</mi></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"></span></p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="Ch1.S1.I1.i3" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S1.I1.i3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.S1.I1.i3.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\forall g\in G,e\cdot g=g\cdot e=g" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo rspace="0.167em">∀</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>e</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>e</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"></span></p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem2" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 1.1.2</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">A subgroup <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H&lt;G" display="inline"><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo>&lt;</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow></math> of group <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem2.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G" display="inline"><mi>G</mi></math> is a subset that is also a group.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_example">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Example 1.1.3</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">Consider the group <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(\mathbb{Z},0,+)" display="inline"><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>ℤ</mi><mo>,</mo><mn>0</mn><mo rspace="0em">,</mo><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">+</mo><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></math>, and a subgroup <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H&lt;\mathbb{Z}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo>&lt;</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow></math>.
We show that <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H=n\mathbb{Z}=\left\{{nm\mid m\in\mathbb{Z}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n\geq 0" display="inline"><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>≥</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">If <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H=\left\{{0}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, then we can write <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H=0\mathbb{Z}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mn>0</mn><mo>⁢</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
Otherwise, consider the set <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p2.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="X=\left\{{h\in H\mid h&gt;0}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>X</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>H</mi></mrow><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>&gt;</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, which is non-empty by assumption.
Pick <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p2.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n=\min X" display="inline"><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>min</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>X</mi></mrow></mrow></math> (by well-ordering), and for a given <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p2.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="h\in H" display="inline"><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>H</mi></mrow></math>, factor it as <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p2.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="h=nq+r" display="inline"><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>q</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mi>r</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p2.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="0\leq r&lt;n" display="inline"><mrow><mn>0</mn><mo>≤</mo><mi>r</mi><mo>&lt;</mo><mi>n</mi></mrow></math>.
Thus, <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p2.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="r\in H" display="inline"><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>H</mi></mrow></math>, by closure, but <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p2.m9" class="ltx_Math" alttext="r\not\in X" display="inline"><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>∉</mo><mi>X</mi></mrow></math>, thus <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p2.m10" class="ltx_Math" alttext="r=0" display="inline"><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p2.m11" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H\subset n\mathbb{Z}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo>⊂</mo><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
Moreover, <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p2.m12" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n\mathbb{Z}\subset H" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow><mo>⊂</mo><mi>H</mi></mrow></math>, since <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem3.p2.m13" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n\in H" display="inline"><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>H</mi></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem4" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 1.1.4</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem4.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">A <em class="ltx_emph ltx_font_upright">group action</em> is an operation <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem4.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G\times XtoX" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>G</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>X</mi></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>t</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>o</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>X</mi></mrow></math>, s.t.</span></p>
<ul id="Ch1.S1.I2" class="ltx_itemize">
<li id="Ch1.S1.I2.i1" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S1.I2.i1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.S1.I2.i1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\forall h,g\in G,x\in X,h\cdot(g\cdot x)=(hg)\cdot x" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo rspace="0.167em">∀</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo>,</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>X</mi></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow><mo rspace="0.055em" stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"></span></p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="Ch1.S1.I2.i2" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S1.I2.i2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.S1.I2.i2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\forall x\in X,e\cdot x=x" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo rspace="0.167em">∀</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mi>X</mi></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>e</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"></span></p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">We say <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem4.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G" display="inline"><mi>G</mi></math> acts on <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem4.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="X" display="inline"><mi>X</mi></math> (through an action <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem4.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\cdot" display="inline"><mo>⋅</mo></math>)</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.SS1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Groups interact with sets through actions.
Through actions, we can find equivalences in such sets.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem5" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 1.1.5</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem5.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">If <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem5.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G" display="inline"><mi>G</mi></math> acts on <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem5.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="X" display="inline"><mi>X</mi></math>, then the <em class="ltx_emph ltx_font_upright">orbit</em> of <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem5.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x\in X" display="inline"><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>X</mi></mrow></math> is <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem5.p1.m4" class="ltx_math_unparsed" alttext="\llbracket x\rrbracket=\left\{{g\cdot x\mid g\in g}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟦</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟧</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0.167em">∣</mo><mi>g</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>g</mi><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem6" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 1.1.6</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem6.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">If <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem6.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G" display="inline"><mi>G</mi></math> acts on <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem6.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="X" display="inline"><mi>X</mi></math>, then <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem6.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x\sim y\iff x=g\cdot y" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>∼</mo><mi>y</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">⇔</mo><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>y</mi></mrow></mrow></mrow></math> is an equivalence relation.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.SS1.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We check the properties:</p>
<ul id="Ch1.S1.I3" class="ltx_itemize">
<li id="Ch1.S1.I3.i1" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S1.I3.i1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Reflective: <math id="Ch1.S1.I3.i1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x\sim x" display="inline"><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>∼</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></math>, since <math id="Ch1.S1.I3.i1.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="e\cdot x=x" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>e</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></math></p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="Ch1.S1.I3.i2" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S1.I3.i2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Symmetric: <math id="Ch1.S1.I3.i2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x\sim y" display="inline"><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>∼</mo><mi>y</mi></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch1.S1.I3.i2.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x=g\cdot y" display="inline"><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>y</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, and <math id="Ch1.S1.I3.i2.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="y=e\cdot y=(g^{-1}g)\cdot y=g^{-1}\cdot(g\cdot y)=g\cdot x" display="inline"><mrow><mi>y</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>e</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>y</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msup><mi>g</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup><mo>⁢</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow><mo rspace="0.055em" stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>y</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msup><mi>g</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>y</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></mrow></math></p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="Ch1.S1.I3.i3" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S1.I3.i3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Transitive: <math id="Ch1.S1.I3.i3.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x\sim y" display="inline"><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>∼</mo><mi>y</mi></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch1.S1.I3.i3.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="y\sim z" display="inline"><mrow><mi>y</mi><mo>∼</mo><mi>z</mi></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch1.S1.I3.i3.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="y=g\cdot x" display="inline"><mrow><mi>y</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, <math id="Ch1.S1.I3.i3.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z=h\cdot y" display="inline"><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>y</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, and <math id="Ch1.S1.I3.i3.p1.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z=h\cdot(g\cdot x)=(hg)\cdot x" display="inline"><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow><mo rspace="0.055em" stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></mrow></math></p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
<p class="ltx_p">∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.SS1.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Thus, we find that the orbits <em class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">partition</em> the set into equivalence classes.
This observation is central towards our results for this section.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.SS1.p4" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">An important example is when <math id="Ch1.S1.SS1.p4.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G" display="inline"><mi>G</mi></math>, or <math id="Ch1.S1.SS1.p4.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H&lt;G" display="inline"><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo>&lt;</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow></math> is acting on itself, through the group operation (or as we will later see, with conjugation).</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem7" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_example">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Example 1.1.7</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem7.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">Let <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem7.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H&lt;G" display="inline"><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo>&lt;</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow></math> be a subgroup. Then <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem7.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H" display="inline"><mi>H</mi></math> acts on <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem7.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G" display="inline"><mi>G</mi></math>, <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem7.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="h\cdot g\mapsto hg" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">↦</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
Moreover, <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem7.p1.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a\sim b\iff a=hb\iff ab^{-1}=h\iff ab^{-1}\in H" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>∼</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">⇔</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">⇔</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msup><mi>b</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">⇔</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msup><mi>b</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mi>H</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
Oftentimes, we write this as <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem7.p1.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H\cdot g=\left\{{h\cdot g\mid h\in H}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>H</mi></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math>.
In this case, we also call the orbits <em class="ltx_emph ltx_font_upright">cosets</em>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.SS1.p5" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">This idea of equivalence classes also lends itself to <em class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">quotients</em>.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem8" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 1.1.8</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem8.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">Suppose <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem8.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H&lt;G" display="inline"><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo>&lt;</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow></math>, <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem8.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H" display="inline"><mi>H</mi></math> acts on <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem8.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G" display="inline"><mi>G</mi></math>.
Then, <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem8.p1.m4" class="ltx_math_unparsed" alttext="G/H=\left\{{\llbracket g\rrbracket\mid g\in G}\right\}=\left\{{H\cdot g\mid g%
\in G}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>G</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>H</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟦</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟧</mo></mrow><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0.167em">∣</mo><mi>g</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>G</mi><mo>}</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mi>H</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0.167em">∣</mo><mi>g</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>G</mi><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem9" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_example">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Example 1.1.9</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem9.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">Consider the groups of integers under addition, <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem9.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(\mathbb{Z},0,+)" display="inline"><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>ℤ</mi><mo>,</mo><mn>0</mn><mo rspace="0em">,</mo><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">+</mo><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem9.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n\mathbb{Z}=\left\{{nm\mid m\in\mathbb{Z}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math>.
Then,</span></p>
<table id="Ch1.Ex1" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_center"><math id="Ch1.Ex1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbb{Z}/n\mathbb{Z}=\left\{{n\mathbb{Z}\cdot m\mid m\in\mathbb{Z}}\right\}=%
\left\{{n\mathbb{Z}\cdot m\mid 0\leq m&lt;n}\right\}\coloneq\mathbb{Z}_{n}" display="block"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>ℤ</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>n</mi></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><mn>0</mn><mo>≤</mo><mi>m</mi><mo>&lt;</mo><mi>n</mi></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow><mo>≔</mo><msub><mi>ℤ</mi><mi>n</mi></msub></mrow></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem10" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_example">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Example 1.1.10</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">We might ask when a quotient <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G/H" display="inline"><mrow><mi>G</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>H</mi></mrow></math> is a group.
A sufficient condition is called <em class="ltx_emph ltx_font_upright">normality</em>.
We say <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N\triangleleft G" display="inline"><mrow><mi>N</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⊲</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow></math> a normal subgroup if <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="gN=Ng" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>N</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, or that <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="gng^{-1}\in N" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>n</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msup><mi>g</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow></math> for all <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n\in N,g\in G" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
Indeed, if <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N\triangleleft G" display="inline"><mrow><mi>N</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⊲</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow></math>, then the operation <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(gN)(hN)\mapsto(gh)N" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">↦</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow></mrow></math> is a well-defined operation:</span></p>
<ul id="Ch1.S1.I4" class="ltx_itemize">
<li id="Ch1.S1.I4.i1" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S1.I4.i1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">If </span><math id="Ch1.S1.I4.i1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="g_{1}N=g_{2}N" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">, then </span><math id="Ch1.S1.I4.i1.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="g_{1}=g_{2}n" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi>n</mi></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">, and </span><math id="Ch1.S1.I4.i1.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="g_{1}h=g_{2}nh=g_{2}(g_{2}^{-1}mg_{2})h=mg_{2}h\in N(g_{2}h)=(g_{2}h)N" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi>n</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msubsup><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msubsup><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mi>N</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">, so </span><math id="Ch1.S1.I4.i1.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="g_{1}hN=g_{2}hN" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi>h</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi>h</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">.</span></p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="Ch1.S1.I4.i2" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S1.I4.i2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.S1.I4.i2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(g_{N})(g^{-1}N)=(gg^{-1})N=N" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>g</mi><mi>N</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msup><mi>g</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup><mo>⁢</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msup><mi>g</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">, so we have inverse and identity elements.</span></p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.SS1.p6" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">In fact, all orbits are also cosets.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem11" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 1.1.11</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem11.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">Let <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem11.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G" display="inline"><mi>G</mi></math> act on <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem11.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="X" display="inline"><mi>X</mi></math>.
Then, for <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem11.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x\in X" display="inline"><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>X</mi></mrow></math>, we write <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem11.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G_{x}\coloneq\left\{{g\in G\mid g\cdot x=x}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>G</mi><mi>x</mi></msub><mo>≔</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, the stabilizer of <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem11.p1.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x" display="inline"><mi>x</mi></math>, and <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem11.p1.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G_{x}&lt;G" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>G</mi><mi>x</mi></msub><mo>&lt;</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow></math> is a subgroup.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem12" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 1.1.12</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem12.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">If <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem12.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G" display="inline"><mi>G</mi></math> acts on <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem12.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="X" display="inline"><mi>X</mi></math>, then <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem12.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G/G_{x}\cong G\cdot x" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>G</mi><mo>/</mo><msub><mi>G</mi><mi>x</mi></msub></mrow><mo>≅</mo><mrow><mi>G</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></mrow></math></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.SS1.p7" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We consider <math id="Ch1.S1.SS1.p7.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f:gG_{x}\mapsto g\cdot x" display="inline"><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>G</mi><mi>x</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">↦</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.
Then, it is a well-defined bijective function, because</p>
<ul id="Ch1.S1.I5" class="ltx_itemize">
<li id="Ch1.S1.I5.i1" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S1.I5.i1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">For <math id="Ch1.S1.I5.i1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="gG_{x}=hG_{x}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>G</mi><mi>x</mi></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>G</mi><mi>x</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></math>, <math id="Ch1.S1.I5.i1.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="g=hs" display="inline"><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>s</mi></mrow></mrow></math> for some <math id="Ch1.S1.I5.i1.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="s\in G_{x}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>s</mi><mo>∈</mo><msub><mi>G</mi><mi>x</mi></msub></mrow></math>, and <math id="Ch1.S1.I5.i1.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f(gG_{x})=g\cdot x=h\cdot(s\cdot x)=h\cdot x=f(hG_{x})" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>G</mi><mi>x</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>s</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>G</mi><mi>x</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="Ch1.S1.I5.i2" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S1.I5.i2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">For <math id="Ch1.S1.I5.i2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="y\in G\cdot x" display="inline"><mrow><mi>y</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mi>G</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch1.S1.I5.i2.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="y=g\cdot x" display="inline"><mrow><mi>y</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, and <math id="Ch1.S1.I5.i2.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f(gG_{x})=y" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>G</mi><mi>x</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>y</mi></mrow></math>.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="Ch1.S1.I5.i3" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S1.I5.i3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">For <math id="Ch1.S1.I5.i3.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f(gG_{x})=f(hG_{x})" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>G</mi><mi>x</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>G</mi><mi>x</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch1.S1.I5.i3.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="g\cdot x=h\cdot x" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, so that <math id="Ch1.S1.I5.i3.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(h^{-1}g)\cdot x=(h^{-1}h)\cdot x=x" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msup><mi>h</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup><mo>⁢</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow><mo rspace="0.055em" stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msup><mi>h</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup><mo>⁢</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo rspace="0.055em" stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></math>, i.e. <math id="Ch1.S1.I5.i3.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="hG_{x}=gG_{x}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>G</mi><mi>x</mi></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>G</mi><mi>x</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></math>.</p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
<p class="ltx_p">∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem13" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_corollary">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Corollary 1.1.13</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem13.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem13.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H&lt;G" display="inline"><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo>&lt;</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">, then the map <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem13.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\phi_{g}:H\to gH" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>ϕ</mi><mi>g</mi></msub><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>H</mi></mrow></mrow></mrow></math> that sends <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem13.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="h\mapsto gh" display="inline"><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo stretchy="false">↦</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow></mrow></math> is bijective.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.SS1.p8" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">The stabilizer <math id="Ch1.S1.SS1.p8.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H_{g}=\left\{{h\in H\mid gh=g}\right\}=\left\{{e}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>H</mi><mi>g</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>H</mi></mrow><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mi>e</mi><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, and so <math id="Ch1.S1.SS1.p8.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H\cong H/\left\{{e}\right\}\cong gH" display="inline"><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo>≅</mo><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo>/</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mi>e</mi><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>≅</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>H</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem14" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_corollary">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Corollary 1.1.14</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem14.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem14.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H&lt;G" display="inline"><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo>&lt;</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">, then <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem14.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left|{G}\right|=\left|{H}\right|\cdot\left|{G/H}\right|" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo>|</mo><mi>G</mi><mo>|</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo>|</mo><mi>H</mi><mo rspace="0.055em">|</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mrow><mo>|</mo><mrow><mi>G</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>H</mi></mrow><mo>|</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.SS1.p9" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We know that <math id="Ch1.S1.SS1.p9.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G/H" display="inline"><mrow><mi>G</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>H</mi></mrow></math> are a collection of equally sized orbits that partition the set.
Thus, the size of the set is a product of the size of each orbit <math id="Ch1.S1.SS1.p9.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left|{H}\right|" display="inline"><mrow><mo>|</mo><mi>H</mi><mo>|</mo></mrow></math> with the number of orbits <math id="Ch1.S1.SS1.p9.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left|{G/H}\right|" display="inline"><mrow><mo>|</mo><mrow><mi>G</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>H</mi></mrow><mo>|</mo></mrow></math>.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
</section>
<section id="Ch1.S1.SS2" class="ltx_subsection">
<h4 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">1.1.2 </span>Permutations</h4>

<div id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We demonstrate the use of our technology on the permutation group.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem15" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 1.1.15</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem15.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">The <em class="ltx_emph ltx_font_upright">symmetric</em> group <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem15.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S_{n}=\left\{{f:\mathbb{Z}_{n}\to\mathbb{Z}_{n}\mid f\emph{ bijective }}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>S</mi><mi>n</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mi>f</mi><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><msub><mi>ℤ</mi><mi>n</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mrow><msub><mi>ℤ</mi><mi>n</mi></msub><mo>∣</mo><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mtext><em class="ltx_emph ltx_font_upright"> bijective </em></mtext></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math> is a group under function composition.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem16" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 1.1.16</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem16.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem16.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sigma\in S_{n}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>σ</mi><mo>∈</mo><msub><mi>S</mi><mi>n</mi></msub></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is a <em class="ltx_emph ltx_font_upright">cycle</em> over its range <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem16.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x_{0},x_{1},\ldots,x_{m}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>x</mi><mn>0</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>m</mi></msub></mrow></math> where <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem16.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x_{0}=x_{m}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>x</mi><mn>0</mn></msub><mo>=</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>m</mi></msub></mrow></math>, if</span></p>
<ul id="Ch1.S1.I6" class="ltx_itemize">
<li id="Ch1.S1.I6.i1" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S1.I6.i1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.S1.I6.i1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sigma(x_{i})=x_{i+1}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>σ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>+</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msub></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">, for </span><math id="Ch1.S1.I6.i1.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="0\leq i&lt;m" display="inline"><mrow><mn>0</mn><mo>≤</mo><mi>i</mi><mo>&lt;</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"></span></p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="Ch1.S1.I6.i2" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S1.I6.i2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.S1.I6.i2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sigma(y)=y" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>σ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>y</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>y</mi></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> for </span><math id="Ch1.S1.I6.i2.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="y\neq x_{i}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>y</mi><mo>≠</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"></span></p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem16.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">We say cycles <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem16.p2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sigma,\tau" display="inline"><mrow><mi>σ</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>τ</mi></mrow></math> are <em class="ltx_emph ltx_font_upright">disjoint</em> if their range are disjoint, i.e. <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem16.p2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sigma(m)\neq m\implies\tau(m)=m" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>σ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>≠</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟹</mo><mrow><mi>τ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">The result for this section is to find a representation for the elements in the permutation group,</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem17" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 1.1.17</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem17.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">Every <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem17.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sigma\in S_{n}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>σ</mi><mo>∈</mo><msub><mi>S</mi><mi>n</mi></msub></mrow></math> is a unique product of cycles <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem17.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\tau_{1}\cdots\tau_{m}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>τ</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">⋯</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>τ</mi><mi>m</mi></msub></mrow></math>, up to order of <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem17.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\tau_{i}" display="inline"><msub><mi>τ</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem18" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_lemma">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Lemma 1.1.18</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem18.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">If cycles <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem18.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\tau,\sigma\in S_{n}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>τ</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>σ</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><msub><mi>S</mi><mi>n</mi></msub></mrow></math> are disjoint, they commute.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Consider any <math id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p3.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="m\in\mathbb{Z}_{n}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>∈</mo><msub><mi>ℤ</mi><mi>n</mi></msub></mrow></math>, and assume WLOG that <math id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p3.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\tau(x)\neq x" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>τ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>≠</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></math> (and so, <math id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sigma(x)=x" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>σ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></math>).
First, <math id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p3.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\tau\circ\sigma(x)=\tau(x)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>τ</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">∘</mo><mi>σ</mi></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>τ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.
Moreover, since <math id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p3.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\tau" display="inline"><mi>τ</mi></math> is injective, then <math id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p3.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\tau(\tau(x))\neq\tau(x)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>τ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>τ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>≠</mo><mrow><mi>τ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, so <math id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p3.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sigma(\tau(x))=\tau(x)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>σ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>τ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>τ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, and <math id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p3.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sigma\circ\tau(x)=\tau(x)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>σ</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">∘</mo><mi>τ</mi></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>τ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem19" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_lemma">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Lemma 1.1.19</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem19.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">If <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem19.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbb{Z}" display="inline"><mi>ℤ</mi></math> acts on <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem19.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbb{Z}_{n}" display="inline"><msub><mi>ℤ</mi><mi>n</mi></msub></math>, then for all <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem19.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x\in X" display="inline"><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>X</mi></mrow></math>, <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem19.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbb{Z}\cdot x\cong Z_{m}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>ℤ</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo>≅</mo><msub><mi>Z</mi><mi>m</mi></msub></mrow></math> for some <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem19.p1.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="m" display="inline"><mi>m</mi></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p4" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Since <math id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p4.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbb{Z}_{x}&lt;\mathbb{Z}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>ℤ</mi><mi>x</mi></msub><mo>&lt;</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow></math> is a subgroup, then <math id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p4.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbb{Z}_{x}=m\mathbb{Z}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>ℤ</mi><mi>x</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow></mrow></math> for some <math id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p4.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="m" display="inline"><mi>m</mi></math>, and <math id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbb{Z}\cdot x\cong\mathbb{Z}/m\mathbb{Z}\cong\mathbb{Z}_{m}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>ℤ</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo>≅</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>ℤ</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow><mo>≅</mo><msub><mi>ℤ</mi><mi>m</mi></msub></mrow></math>.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p5" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Now, we prove the decomposition theorem on permutations:</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">
<a href="#Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem17" title="Theorem 1.1.17. ‣ 1.1.2 Permutations ‣ 1.1 Groups and Actions ‣ Chapter 1 Group Theory ‣ MATH 427 Notes" class="ltx_ref"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">1.1.17</span></a>.</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p6" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We prove existence and uniqueness separately.</p>
<ul id="Ch1.S1.I7" class="ltx_itemize">
<li id="Ch1.S1.I7.i1" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S1.I7.i1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><em class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">existence</em>:
Consider an action <math id="Ch1.S1.I7.i1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbb{Z}" display="inline"><mi>ℤ</mi></math> on <math id="Ch1.S1.I7.i1.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbb{Z}_{n}" display="inline"><msub><mi>ℤ</mi><mi>n</mi></msub></math>, where <math id="Ch1.S1.I7.i1.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p\cdot q\mapsto\sigma^{p}(q)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>p</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>q</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">↦</mo><mrow><msup><mi>σ</mi><mi>p</mi></msup><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>q</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.
Then, for every orbit <math id="Ch1.S1.I7.i1.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\llbracket s\rrbracket" display="inline"><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟦</mo><mi>s</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟧</mo></mrow></math>, we consider the cycle</p>
<table id="Ch1.Ex2" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_center"><math id="Ch1.Ex2.m1" class="ltx_math_unparsed" alttext="\sigma_{s}(r)=\begin{cases}r&amp;r\not\in\llbracket s\rrbracket\\
\sigma^{t}(r)&amp;\text{otherwise}\end{cases}" display="block"><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>σ</mi><mi>s</mi></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>r</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mtable columnspacing="5pt" displaystyle="true" rowspacing="0pt"><mtr><mtd class="ltx_align_left" columnalign="left"><mi>r</mi></mtd><mtd class="ltx_align_left" columnalign="left"><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>∉</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟦</mo><mi>s</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟧</mo></mrow></mrow></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd class="ltx_align_left" columnalign="left"><mrow><msup><mi>σ</mi><mi>t</mi></msup><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>r</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mtd><mtd class="ltx_align_left" columnalign="left"><mtext>otherwise</mtext></mtd></mtr></mtable></mrow></mrow></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p class="ltx_p">Choosing <math id="Ch1.S1.I7.i1.p1.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="s_{1},\ldots,s_{m}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>s</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>s</mi><mi>m</mi></msub></mrow></math> representatives for the orbits, then <math id="Ch1.S1.I7.i1.p1.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sigma_{s_{1}}\cdots\sigma_{s_{m}}=\sigma" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>σ</mi><msub><mi>s</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">⋯</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>σ</mi><msub><mi>s</mi><mi>m</mi></msub></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>σ</mi></mrow></math> is our representation.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="Ch1.S1.I7.i2" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S1.I7.i2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><em class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">uniqueness</em>:
Any decomposition of <math id="Ch1.S1.I7.i2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sigma" display="inline"><mi>σ</mi></math> into cycles induces a partition into orbits, so every decomposition can be formed in the above process.
Moreover, since these are exactly the orbits of <math id="Ch1.S1.I7.i2.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sigma" display="inline"><mi>σ</mi></math>, every decomposition is the same.</p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
<p class="ltx_p">∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem20" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_corollary">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Corollary 1.1.20</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem20.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">Every permutation <math id="Ch1.S1.Thmtheorem20.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sigma\in S_{n}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>σ</mi><mo>∈</mo><msub><mi>S</mi><mi>n</mi></msub></mrow></math> is a product of transpositions (i.e. cycles of order 2).</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p7" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">It is sufficient to prove for cycles.
Indeed, a cycle <math id="Ch1.S1.SS2.p7.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(n_{1}\ldots n_{m})=(n_{1}n_{2})\cdots(n_{m-1}n_{m})" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>n</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>n</mi><mi>m</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>n</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>n</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">⋯</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>n</mi><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>n</mi><mi>m</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section id="Ch1.S2" class="ltx_section">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">1.2 </span>Group Homomorphisms</h3>

<div id="Ch1.S2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We turn out attention to studying groups and the relationship between groups (instead of how groups interact with other objects).
Our primary tool describing such relationship is the homomorphism.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="Ch1.Sx1" class="ltx_section">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">Homomorphism Properties</h3>

<div id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem1" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 1.2.1</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f:G\to H" display="inline"><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><mi>G</mi><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mi>H</mi></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is a <em class="ltx_emph ltx_font_upright">homomorphism</em> if for all <math id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem1.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="g,h\in G" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow></math>, <math id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem1.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f(gh)=f(g)f(h)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>h</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem2" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 1.2.2</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">An <em class="ltx_emph ltx_font_upright">isomorphism</em> is a bijective homomorphism.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem3" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_lemma">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Lemma 1.2.3</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem3.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f(e_{G})=e_{H}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mi>G</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mi>H</mi></msub></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.Sx1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="e_{H}=f(e_{G})^{-1}f(e_{G})=f(e_{G})^{-1}f(e_{G}e_{G})=f(e_{G})" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>e</mi><mi>H</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mi>G</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup><mo>⁢</mo><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mi>G</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mi>G</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup><mo>⁢</mo><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>e</mi><mi>G</mi></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mi>G</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mi>G</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem4" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_lemma">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Lemma 1.2.4</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem4.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">If <math id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem4.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f" display="inline"><mi>f</mi></math> is an isomorphism, then <math id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem4.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f^{-1}" display="inline"><msup><mi>f</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup></math> is a homomorphism.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Let <math id="Ch1.Sx1.p2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a=f(a_{0}),b=f(b_{0})" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>a</mi><mn>0</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>b</mi><mn>0</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, so that <math id="Ch1.Sx1.p2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f^{-1}(ab)=f^{-1}(f(a_{0})f(b_{0}))=f^{-1}f(a_{0}b_{0})=a_{0}b_{0}=f^{-1}(a)f^%
{-1}(b)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><msup><mi>f</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msup><mi>f</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>a</mi><mn>0</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>b</mi><mn>0</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msup><mi>f</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup><mo>⁢</mo><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>a</mi><mn>0</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>b</mi><mn>0</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mi>a</mi><mn>0</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>b</mi><mn>0</mn></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msup><mi>f</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>a</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><msup><mi>f</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>b</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Now, we make the relationship between homomorphisms and actions clear.
First, observe that <math id="Ch1.Sx1.p3.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathop{Hom}(G,H)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>o</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>G</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>H</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, the set of homomorphisms between <math id="Ch1.Sx1.p3.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G" display="inline"><mi>G</mi></math> and <math id="Ch1.Sx1.p3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H" display="inline"><mi>H</mi></math>, and <math id="Ch1.Sx1.p3.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathop{Aut}(G)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>A</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>u</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>t</mi></mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>G</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, the set of isomorphisms from <math id="Ch1.Sx1.p3.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G" display="inline"><mi>G</mi></math> to <math id="Ch1.Sx1.p3.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G" display="inline"><mi>G</mi></math> are groups under composition.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem5" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_example">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Example 1.2.5</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem5.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">We show that (some) actions are equivalently homomorphisms between <math id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem5.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G" display="inline"><mi>G</mi></math> to an automorphism group.</span></p>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem5.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">If <math id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem5.p2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G" display="inline"><mi>G</mi></math> acts on <math id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem5.p2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="H" display="inline"><mi>H</mi></math> with <math id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem5.p2.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="g\cdot(h_{1}h_{2})=(g\cdot h_{1})(g\cdot h_{2})" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>h</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>h</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><msub><mi>h</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><msub><mi>h</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, then consider <math id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem5.p2.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mu:G\to\mathop{Aut}(H)" display="inline"><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><mi>G</mi><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>A</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>u</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>t</mi></mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>H</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, where <math id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem5.p2.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mu(g):h\to g\cdot h" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>g</mi><mo rspace="0.278em" stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.
Indeed, it a homomorphism, since</span></p>
<ul id="Ch1.Sx1.I1" class="ltx_itemize">
<li id="Ch1.Sx1.I1.i1" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.I1.i1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.Sx1.I1.i1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mu(g)" display="inline"><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is a homomorphism: </span><math id="Ch1.Sx1.I1.i1.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mu(g)(h_{1}h_{2})=g\cdot(h_{1}h_{2})=(g\cdot h_{1})(g\cdot h_{2})=\mu(g)(h_{1%
})\mu(g)(h_{2})" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>h</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>h</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>h</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>h</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><msub><mi>h</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><msub><mi>h</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>h</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>μ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>h</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"></span></p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="Ch1.Sx1.I1.i2" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.I1.i2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.Sx1.I1.i2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mu(g)" display="inline"><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is an automorphism Since it is surjective (</span><math id="Ch1.Sx1.I1.i2.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="h=\mu(g)(g^{-1}\cdot h)" display="inline"><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msup><mi>g</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">) and therefore injective.</span></p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="Ch1.Sx1.I1.i3" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.I1.i3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.Sx1.I1.i3.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mu" display="inline"><mi>μ</mi></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is a homomorphism: </span><math id="Ch1.Sx1.I1.i3.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mu(g_{1}g_{2})(h)=(g_{1}g_{2})\cdot h=g_{1}\cdot(g_{2}\cdot h)=\mu(g_{1})%
\circ\mu(g_{2})(h)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>h</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo rspace="0.055em" stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo rspace="0.055em" stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="0.222em">∘</mo><mi>μ</mi></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>h</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">.</span></p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem5.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">Conversely, if we have a homomorphism <math id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem5.p3.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mu:G\to\mathop{Aut}(H)" display="inline"><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><mi>G</mi><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>A</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>u</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>t</mi></mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>H</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, then we define the action <math id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem5.p3.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="g\cdot h=\mu(g)(h)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>h</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, where indeed,</span></p>
<ul id="Ch1.Sx1.I2" class="ltx_itemize">
<li id="Ch1.Sx1.I2.i1" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.I2.i1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.Sx1.I2.i1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="e\cdot h=\mu(e)(h)=\mathop{id}(h)=h" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>e</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>e</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>h</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>d</mi></mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>h</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"></span></p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="Ch1.Sx1.I2.i2" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.I2.i2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.Sx1.I2.i2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="g_{1}\cdot(g_{2}\cdot h)=\mu(g_{1})\mu(g_{2})(h)=\mu(g_{1}g_{2})(h)=(g_{1}g_{2%
})\cdot h" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>μ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>h</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>μ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>h</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>g</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo rspace="0.055em" stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><mi>h</mi></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"></span></p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.p4" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Finally, we mention important subgroups induced by a homomorphism.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem6" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 1.2.6</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.Sx1.Thmtheorem6.p1" class="ltx_para">
