Choose <math id="Ch1.S3.SS3.p3.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="e\neq g\in G^{G}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>e</mi><mo>≠</mo><mi>g</mi><mo>∈</mo><msup><mi>G</mi><mi>G</mi></msup></mrow></math>, and <math id="Ch1.S3.SS3.p3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="h\in G\setminus G^{G}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>h</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mi>G</mi><mo>∖</mo><msup><mi>G</mi><mi>G</mi></msup></mrow></mrow></math>.
Indeed, <math id="Ch1.S3.SS3.p3.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle g\rangle&lt;G^{G}\triangleleft G" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>&lt;</mo><mrow><msup><mi>G</mi><mi>G</mi></msup><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⊲</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S3.SS3.p4" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Now, we verify that</p>
<ul id="Ch1.S3.I3" class="ltx_itemize">
<li id="Ch1.S3.I3.i1" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S3.I3.i1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.S3.I3.i1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle h\rangle\cap\langle g\rangle=\left\{{e}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>h</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>∩</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mi>e</mi><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, since <math id="Ch1.S3.I3.i1.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left|{\langle h\rangle\cap\langle g\rangle}\right|\mid p" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo>|</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>h</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>∩</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>|</mo></mrow><mo>∣</mo><mi>p</mi></mrow></math> but <math id="Ch1.S3.I3.i1.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle h\rangle\not\subset\langle g\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>h</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>⊄</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math>.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="Ch1.S3.I3.i2" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S3.I3.i2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.S3.I3.i2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle h\rangle\langle g\rangle=G" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>h</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow></math>, since the map <math id="Ch1.S3.I3.i2.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\pi:(h^{k},g^{\ell})\mapsto h^{k}g^{\ell}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>π</mi><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msup><mi>h</mi><mi>k</mi></msup><mo>,</mo><msup><mi>g</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">ℓ</mi></msup><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo stretchy="false">↦</mo><mrow><msup><mi>h</mi><mi>k</mi></msup><mo>⁢</mo><msup><mi>g</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">ℓ</mi></msup></mrow></mrow></mrow></math> is injective.</p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
<p class="ltx_p">∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch1.S3.Thmtheorem12" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 1.3.12</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S3.Thmtheorem12.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">If <math id="Ch1.S3.Thmtheorem12.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left|{G}\right|=pq" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo>|</mo><mi>G</mi><mo>|</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>p</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>q</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, <math id="Ch1.S3.Thmtheorem12.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p&gt;q" display="inline"><mrow><mi>p</mi><mo>&gt;</mo><mi>q</mi></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch1.S3.Thmtheorem12.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="G\cong\mathbb{Z}_{p}\rtimes\mathbb{Z}_{q}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>G</mi><mo>≅</mo><mrow><msub><mi>ℤ</mi><mi>p</mi></msub><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋊</mo><msub><mi>ℤ</mi><mi>q</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch1.S3.SS3.p5" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Consider <math id="Ch1.S3.SS3.p5.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="P,Q" display="inline"><mrow><mi>P</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>Q</mi></mrow></math> subgroups of order <math id="Ch1.S3.SS3.p5.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p" display="inline"><mi>p</mi></math> and <math id="Ch1.S3.SS3.p5.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="q" display="inline"><mi>q</mi></math> respectively.
We know that <math id="Ch1.S3.SS3.p5.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n_{p}\mid q" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>n</mi><mi>p</mi></msub><mo>∣</mo><mi>q</mi></mrow></math>, and since <math id="Ch1.S3.SS3.p5.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n_{p}\equiv_{p}1" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>n</mi><mi>p</mi></msub><msub><mo>≡</mo><mi>p</mi></msub><mn>1</mn></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch1.S3.SS3.p5.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n_{p}=1" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>n</mi><mi>p</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></math>.
Thus,</p>
<ul id="Ch1.S3.I4" class="ltx_itemize">
<li id="Ch1.S3.I4.i1" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S3.I4.i1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.S3.I4.i1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="P\triangleleft G" display="inline"><mrow><mi>P</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⊲</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow></math>, since <math id="Ch1.S3.I4.i1.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="gPg^{-1}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>P</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msup><mi>g</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup></mrow></math> is p-Sylow (conjugation is iso), and so <math id="Ch1.S3.I4.i1.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="gPg^{-1}=P" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>P</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msup><mi>g</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>P</mi></mrow></math></p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="Ch1.S3.I4.i2" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S3.I4.i2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.S3.I4.i2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="P\cap Q=\left\{{e}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>P</mi><mo>∩</mo><mi>Q</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mi>e</mi><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, since <math id="Ch1.S3.I4.i2.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left|{P\cap Q}\right|\leq\gcd(p,q)=1" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo>|</mo><mrow><mi>P</mi><mo>∩</mo><mi>Q</mi></mrow><mo>|</mo></mrow><mo>≤</mo><mrow><mi>gcd</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>p</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>q</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></math></p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="Ch1.S3.I4.i3" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span> 
<div id="Ch1.S3.I4.i3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch1.S3.I4.i3.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="PQ=G" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>P</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>Q</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow></math>, since <math id="Ch1.S3.I4.i3.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="PQ/P\cong Q/(Q\cap P)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>P</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>Q</mi></mrow><mo>/</mo><mi>P</mi></mrow><mo>≅</mo><mrow><mi>Q</mi><mo>/</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>Q</mi><mo>∩</mo><mi>P</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math> and so <math id="Ch1.S3.I4.i3.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left|{PQ}\right|=\left|{P}\right|\left|{Q}\right|=\left|{G}\right|" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo>|</mo><mrow><mi>P</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>Q</mi></mrow><mo>|</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo>|</mo><mi>P</mi><mo>|</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo>|</mo><mi>Q</mi><mo>|</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>|</mo><mi>G</mi><mo>|</mo></mrow></mrow></math>.</p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
<p class="ltx_p">∎</p>
</div>
</div>
</section>
</section>
</section>
<section id="Ch2" class="ltx_chapter">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_chapter">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_chapter">Chapter 2 </span>Ring Theory</h2>

<section id="Ch2.S1" class="ltx_section">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">2.1 </span>Integers</h3>

<div id="Ch2.S1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We outline our path on the integers.
First, recall this useful property of the integers.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem1" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 2.1.1</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">For every <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a,b\in\mathbb{Z}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow></math> where <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem1.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b\neq 0" display="inline"><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>≠</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>, we can factor <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem1.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a=bq+r" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>q</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mi>r</mi></mrow></mrow></math> s.t. <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem1.p1.m4" class="ltx_math_unparsed" alttext="0\leq\left|\bigr{.}r\right|&lt;\left|\bigr{.}b\right|" display="inline"><mrow><mn>0</mn><mo rspace="0em">≤</mo><mo fence="false">|</mo><mo lspace="0.167em" mathsize="1.200em" rspace="0.167em">.</mo><mi>r</mi><mo fence="false">|</mo><mo lspace="0.167em" rspace="0em">&lt;</mo><mo fence="false">|</mo><mo lspace="0.167em" mathsize="1.200em" rspace="0.167em">.</mo><mi>b</mi><mo fence="false">|</mo></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S1.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Consider <math id="Ch2.S1.p2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="q=\lfloor\frac{a}{b}\rfloor" display="inline"><mrow><mi>q</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⌊</mo><mfrac><mi>a</mi><mi>b</mi></mfrac><mo stretchy="false">⌋</mo></mrow></mrow></math>.
Then, <math id="Ch2.S1.p2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="r=a-bq" display="inline"><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>−</mo><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>q</mi></mrow></mrow></mrow></math> satisifes the inequality.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">From the division algorithm, we work towards a decomposition of integers into prime factors.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem2" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 2.1.2</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">We say <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n" display="inline"><mi>n</mi></math> divides <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem2.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="m" display="inline"><mi>m</mi></math>, denoted as <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem2.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n\mid m" display="inline"><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>∣</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow></math> if <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem2.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="m=nq" display="inline"><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>q</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem3" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 2.1.3</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">The <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem3.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="1\leq d=\gcd(a,b)" display="inline"><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>≤</mo><mi>d</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>gcd</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>a</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>b</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math> if <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem3.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="d\mid a" display="inline"><mrow><mi>d</mi><mo>∣</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow></math>, <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem3.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="d\mid b" display="inline"><mrow><mi>d</mi><mo>∣</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></math>, and moreover for any other <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem3.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c\mid a" display="inline"><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>∣</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow></math>, <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem3.p1.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c\mid b" display="inline"><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>∣</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></math> implies <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem3.p1.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c\mid d" display="inline"><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>∣</mo><mi>d</mi></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.p4" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">For example, for <math id="Ch2.S1.p4.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x\neq 0" display="inline"><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>≠</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S1.p4.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\gcd(0,x)=x" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>gcd</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></math>.
However, note that <math id="Ch2.S1.p4.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\gcd(0,0)" display="inline"><mrow><mi>gcd</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>,</mo><mn>0</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></math> is not defined, since all integers are common divisors.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.p5" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We show that the <math id="Ch2.S1.p5.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\gcd(a,b)" display="inline"><mrow><mi>gcd</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>a</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>b</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></math> is a well-defined function on <math id="Ch2.S1.p5.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a\neq 0" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>≠</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S1.p6" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Let <math id="Ch2.S1.p6.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S=\left\{{ua+vb\mid ua+vb&gt;0}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>S</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>u</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>v</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></mrow><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>u</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>v</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></mrow><mo>&gt;</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math>.
In particular, <math id="Ch2.S1.p6.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a^{2}\in S" display="inline"><mrow><msup><mi>a</mi><mn>2</mn></msup><mo>∈</mo><mi>S</mi></mrow></math>, so <math id="Ch2.S1.p6.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline"><mi>S</mi></math> is non-empty.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.p7" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Now, considering <math id="Ch2.S1.p7.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="d=\min S" display="inline"><mrow><mi>d</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>min</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>S</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, then if <math id="Ch2.S1.p7.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c\mid a" display="inline"><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>∣</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch2.S1.p7.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c\mid b" display="inline"><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>∣</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S1.p7.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c\mid ua+vb=d" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>∣</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>u</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>v</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>d</mi></mrow></math>.
Moreover, for any other <math id="Ch2.S1.p7.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="d^{\prime}" display="inline"><msup><mi>d</mi><mo>′</mo></msup></math> that claims to be the gcd, then <math id="Ch2.S1.p7.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="d^{\prime}\mid d" display="inline"><mrow><msup><mi>d</mi><mo>′</mo></msup><mo>∣</mo><mi>d</mi></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch2.S1.p7.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="d\mid d^{\prime}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>d</mi><mo>∣</mo><msup><mi>d</mi><mo>′</mo></msup></mrow></math> shows that <math id="Ch2.S1.p7.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="d=d^{\prime}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>d</mi><mo>=</mo><msup><mi>d</mi><mo>′</mo></msup></mrow></math> (since positive).
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem4" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 2.1.4</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem4.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">We say <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem4.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x" display="inline"><mi>x</mi></math> is a unit if <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem4.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="xy=1" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>y</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></math> for some <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem4.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="y" display="inline"><mi>y</mi></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem5" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 2.1.5</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem5.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">We say <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem5.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x" display="inline"><mi>x</mi></math> is an irreducible if <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem5.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x=ab" display="inline"><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></mrow></math> only when <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem5.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a" display="inline"><mi>a</mi></math> or <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem5.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b" display="inline"><mi>b</mi></math> is a unit.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem6" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 2.1.6</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem6.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">We say <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem6.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a" display="inline"><mi>a</mi></math> and <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem6.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b" display="inline"><mi>b</mi></math> are coprime if <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem6.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a\mid bx\implies a\mid x" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>∣</mo><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟹</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>∣</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
Moreover, <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem6.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p" display="inline"><mi>p</mi></math> is prime if <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem6.p1.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p" display="inline"><mi>p</mi></math> is coprime with every other integer.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.p8" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Now, we relate these concepts.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem7" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 2.1.7</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem7.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem7.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a" display="inline"><mi>a</mi></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> and <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem7.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b" display="inline"><mi>b</mi></math> are coprime if and only if <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem7.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\gcd(a,b)=1" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>gcd</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>a</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>b</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S1.p9" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Suppose <math id="Ch2.S1.p9.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\gcd(a,b)=1" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>gcd</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>a</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>b</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></math>, i.e. we can find <math id="Ch2.S1.p9.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="ax+by=1" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>y</mi></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></math>.
Then, when <math id="Ch2.S1.p9.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a\mid bc" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>∣</mo><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S1.p9.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a\mid(a(xc)+bc(y))=(ax+by)c=c" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>∣</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>y</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>y</mi></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow></math>.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.p10" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Conversely, if <math id="Ch2.S1.p10.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a" display="inline"><mi>a</mi></math> and <math id="Ch2.S1.p10.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b" display="inline"><mi>b</mi></math> are coprime, then let <math id="Ch2.S1.p10.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="d" display="inline"><mi>d</mi></math> be a common divisor, so that <math id="Ch2.S1.p10.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a=xd" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>d</mi></mrow></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch2.S1.p10.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b=yd" display="inline"><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>y</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>d</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
Now, since <math id="Ch2.S1.p10.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a\mid ya=xyd=bx" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>∣</mo><mrow><mi>y</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>y</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>d</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S1.p10.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a\mid x" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>∣</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></math>.
But also, <math id="Ch2.S1.p10.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x\mid a" display="inline"><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>∣</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow></math>, so <math id="Ch2.S1.p10.m9" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x=\pm a" display="inline"><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>±</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch2.S1.p10.m10" class="ltx_Math" alttext="d=\pm 1" display="inline"><mrow><mi>d</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>±</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></mrow></math>.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem8" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 2.1.8</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem8.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem8.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p" display="inline"><mi>p</mi></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is prime if and only if <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem8.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p" display="inline"><mi>p</mi></math> is irreducible.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S1.p11" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Suppose <math id="Ch2.S1.p11.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p" display="inline"><mi>p</mi></math> is prime, and write <math id="Ch2.S1.p11.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p=ab" display="inline"><mrow><mi>p</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, i.e. <math id="Ch2.S1.p11.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p\mid ab" display="inline"><mrow><mi>p</mi><mo>∣</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
WLOG, assume that <math id="Ch2.S1.p11.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p\mid a" display="inline"><mrow><mi>p</mi><mo>∣</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow></math>, and since <math id="Ch2.S1.p11.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a\mid p" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>∣</mo><mi>p</mi></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S1.p11.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a=\pm p" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>±</mo><mi>p</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, i.e. <math id="Ch2.S1.p11.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b=\pm 1" display="inline"><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>±</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch2.S1.p11.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b" display="inline"><mi>b</mi></math> is a unit.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.p12" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Conversely, suppose <math id="Ch2.S1.p12.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p" display="inline"><mi>p</mi></math> is irreducible and let <math id="Ch2.S1.p12.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p\mid ab" display="inline"><mrow><mi>p</mi><mo>∣</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
Then, since the only divisors of <math id="Ch2.S1.p12.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p" display="inline"><mi>p</mi></math> are <math id="Ch2.S1.p12.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\pm 1" display="inline"><mrow><mo>±</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></math> or <math id="Ch2.S1.p12.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\pm p" display="inline"><mrow><mo>±</mo><mi>p</mi></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S1.p12.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\gcd(p,a)=1" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>gcd</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>p</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>a</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></math> or <math id="Ch2.S1.p12.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\gcd(p,a)=p" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>gcd</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>p</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>a</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>p</mi></mrow></math>.
If <math id="Ch2.S1.p12.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\gcd(p,a)=1" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>gcd</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>p</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>a</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S1.p12.m9" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a" display="inline"><mi>a</mi></math> and <math id="Ch2.S1.p12.m10" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p" display="inline"><mi>p</mi></math> are coprime, and so <math id="Ch2.S1.p12.m11" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p\mid ab\implies p\mid b" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>p</mi><mo>∣</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟹</mo><mrow><mi>p</mi><mo>∣</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
Otherwise, if <math id="Ch2.S1.p12.m12" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\gcd(p,a)=p" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>gcd</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>p</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>a</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>p</mi></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S1.p12.m13" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a=\pm p" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>±</mo><mi>p</mi></mrow></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch2.S1.p12.m14" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p\mid a" display="inline"><mrow><mi>p</mi><mo>∣</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow></math>.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.p13" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Now, we can talk about factorization into irreducibles, i.e. primes.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem9" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 2.1.9</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem9.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem9.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a" display="inline"><mi>a</mi></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> and <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem9.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b" display="inline"><mi>b</mi></math> are associates if <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem9.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a=ub" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>u</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, for <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem9.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="u" display="inline"><mi>u</mi></math> a unit.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem10" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 2.1.10</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">If <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="0\neq a" display="inline"><mrow><mn>0</mn><mo>≠</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow></math> not a unit, then <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a=up_{1}\cdots p_{n}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>u</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>p</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">⋯</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>n</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></math>, where <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="u" display="inline"><mi>u</mi></math> is a unit and <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p_{1},\ldots,p_{n}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>p</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>n</mi></msub></mrow></math> are irreducible.
Moreover, if <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a=vq_{1}\cdots q_{m}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>v</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>q</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">⋯</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>q</mi><mi>m</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n=m" display="inline"><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow></math> and we can reorder <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="q" display="inline"><mi>q</mi></math> with <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="q_{i}" display="inline"><msub><mi>q</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></math> and <math id="Ch2.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1.m9" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p_{i}" display="inline"><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></math> being associates.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S1.p14" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We proceed by induction on <math id="Ch2.S1.p14.m1" class="ltx_math_unparsed" alttext="\left|\bigr{.}a\right|" display="inline"><mrow><mo fence="false">|</mo><mo lspace="0.167em" mathsize="1.200em" rspace="0.167em">.</mo><mi>a</mi><mo fence="false">|</mo></mrow></math>.
If <math id="Ch2.S1.p14.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a" display="inline"><mi>a</mi></math> is an irreducible, then we win.
Otherwise, <math id="Ch2.S1.p14.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a" display="inline"><mi>a</mi></math> is reducible, and writing <math id="Ch2.S1.p14.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a=bc" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, applying the induction hypothesis proves the existence of factorization.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S1.p15" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Arguing uniqueness, we induct on <math id="Ch2.S1.p15.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\max(n,m)" display="inline"><mrow><mi>max</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>n</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></math>.
Since <math id="Ch2.S1.p15.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p_{1}\mid a" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>p</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>∣</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S1.p15.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p_{1}\mid q_{i}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>p</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>∣</mo><msub><mi>q</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></mrow></math>, say <math id="Ch2.S1.p15.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="q_{1}" display="inline"><msub><mi>q</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></math>.
Then, <math id="Ch2.S1.p15.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p_{1}" display="inline"><msub><mi>p</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></math> and <math id="Ch2.S1.p15.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="q_{1}" display="inline"><msub><mi>q</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></math> are associates (since both irreducible), so inducting on <math id="Ch2.S1.p15.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a^{\prime}=v^{\prime}q_{2}\cdots q_{m}=u^{\prime}p_{2}\cdots p_{m}" display="inline"><mrow><msup><mi>a</mi><mo>′</mo></msup><mo>=</mo><mrow><msup><mi>v</mi><mo>′</mo></msup><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>q</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">⋯</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>q</mi><mi>m</mi></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msup><mi>u</mi><mo>′</mo></msup><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>p</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">⋯</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>m</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></math>, we win.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
</section>
<section id="Ch2.S2" class="ltx_section">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">2.2 </span>Domains</h3>

<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem1" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 2.2.1</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">A (commutative) ring <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R" display="inline"><mi>R</mi></math> is an abelian group <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem1.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(R,+,0)" display="inline"><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>R</mi><mo rspace="0em">,</mo><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">+</mo><mo>,</mo><mn>0</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></math> with an operation <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem1.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R\times R\to R" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow></math>,</span></p>
<table id="Ch2.Ex1" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_center"><math id="Ch2.Ex1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="ab=ba\qquad a(b+c)=ab+ac\qquad 1r=r" display="block"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow></mrow><mspace width="2em"></mspace><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow></mrow></mrow><mspace width="2em"></mspace><mrow><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>⁢</mo><mi>r</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>r</mi></mrow></mrow></mrow></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem2" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 2.2.2</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="0\neq r\in R" display="inline"><mrow><mn>0</mn><mo>≠</mo><mi>r</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is a zero-divisor if <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem2.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\exists s\neq 0" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo rspace="0.167em">∃</mo><mi>s</mi></mrow><mo>≠</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math> s.t. <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem2.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="sr=0" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>s</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>r</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem3" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 2.2.3</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">We say <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem3.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R" display="inline"><mi>R</mi></math> is a domain if there are no zero-divisors.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Note that a field is a domain, since units can not be zero-divisors.
Moreover, finite domains are fields, since for <math id="Ch2.S2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a\neq 0" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>≠</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>, we have the bijection <math id="Ch2.S2.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f_{a}:x\mapsto ax" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>f</mi><mi>a</mi></msub><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">↦</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, with <math id="Ch2.S2.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a\cdot f_{a}^{-1}(1)=1" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⋅</mo><msubsup><mi>f</mi><mi>a</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msubsup></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></math>.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Here, we only concern ourselves with domains, since whenever <math id="Ch2.S2.p2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="ab=ac" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow></mrow></math> for <math id="Ch2.S2.p2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a\neq 0" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>≠</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S2.p2.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a(b-c)=0=b-c" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>−</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>−</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, i.e. <math id="Ch2.S2.p2.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b=c" display="inline"><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow></math>.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem4" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 2.2.4</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem4.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">We say <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem4.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R" display="inline"><mi>R</mi></math> is an Euclidean domain with a function <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem4.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\delta:R\setminus\left\{{0}\right\}\to\mathbb{N}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>∖</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mi>ℕ</mi></mrow></mrow></math> s.t. for any <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem4.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a,b\in R" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow></math> with <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem4.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b\neq 0" display="inline"><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>≠</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math></span></p>
<table id="Ch2.Ex2" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_center"><math id="Ch2.Ex2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a=bq+r\qquad\delta(r)&lt;\delta(b)" display="block"><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>q</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mi>r</mi></mrow></mrow><mspace width="2em"></mspace><mrow><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>r</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>&lt;</mo><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>b</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">For convenience, we denote <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem4.p1.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\delta(0)=-\infty" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>0</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>−</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">∞</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem5" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 2.2.5</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem5.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">We say <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem5.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R" display="inline"><mi>R</mi></math> is a unique-factorization domain if <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem5.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\exists!r=up_{1}\cdots p_{n}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo rspace="0.167em">∃</mo><mo>!</mo></mrow><mo>⁡</mo><mi>r</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>u</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>p</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">⋯</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>n</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></math>, up to associates.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">The main result is to show that in general, Euclidean domains are UFDs.
Towards this, we introduce an intermediate concept of <em class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">ideals</em>.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem6" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 2.2.6</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem6.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">An ideal <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem6.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="I\triangleleft R" display="inline"><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⊲</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow></math> is a subgroup where <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem6.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="ri\in I" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>i</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow></math> for all <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem6.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="r\in R" display="inline"><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow></math>, <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem6.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="i\in I" display="inline"><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem7" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 2.2.7</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem7.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem7.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="I" display="inline"><mi>I</mi></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is principal if <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem7.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="I=\langle c\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math> (as a group).
<math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem7.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R" display="inline"><mi>R</mi></math> is a principal ideal domain if all ideals are principal.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.p4" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Considering the subgroup <math id="Ch2.S2.p4.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R/I" display="inline"><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow></math>, it is moreover a ring with the operation <math id="Ch2.S2.p4.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(r+I)(s+I)=rs+I" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>s</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>s</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
We also define the following operations on ideals (generating new ideals):</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem8" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 2.2.8</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem8.p1" class="ltx_para">
<table id="Ch2.Ex3" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_center"><math id="Ch2.Ex3.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="I_{1}+I_{2}=\left\{{i_{1}+i_{2}\mid i_{j}\in I_{j}}\right\}\qquad I_{1}I_{2}=%
\left\{{i_{1}i_{2}\mid i_{j}\in I_{j}}\right\}" display="block"><mrow><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><msub><mi>i</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>∈</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mi>j</mi></msub></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow><mspace width="2em"></mspace><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><msub><mi>i</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>∈</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mi>j</mi></msub></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem9" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_lemma">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Lemma 2.2.9</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem9.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem9.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle c\rangle=Rc=\left\{{rc\mid r\in R}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.p5" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We know <math id="Ch2.S2.p5.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="rc\in\langle c\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, by definition, so <math id="Ch2.S2.p5.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="Rc\subset\langle c\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow><mo>⊂</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math>.
Moreover, <math id="Ch2.S2.p5.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="Rc" display="inline"><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow></math> is an ideal, since <math id="Ch2.S2.p5.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="rc-sc=(r-s)c\in Rc" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow><mo>−</mo><mrow><mi>s</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>−</mo><mi>s</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch2.S2.p5.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="s(rc)=(sr)c\in Rc" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>s</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>s</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>r</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.p6" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Note that the integers are Euclidean domains <math id="Ch2.S2.p6.m1" class="ltx_math_unparsed" alttext="\delta(r)=\left|\bigr{.}r\right|" display="inline"><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>r</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0em">=</mo><mo fence="false">|</mo><mo lspace="0.167em" mathsize="1.200em" rspace="0.167em">.</mo><mi>r</mi><mo fence="false">|</mo></mrow></math>, as well as PIDs (since only subgroups are <math id="Ch2.S2.p6.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n\mathbb{Z}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow></math>), and UFDs.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem10" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 2.2.10</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem10.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">Euclidean Domains are PIDs.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.p7" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Let <math id="Ch2.S2.p7.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="I" display="inline"><mi>I</mi></math> be an ideal.
If <math id="Ch2.S2.p7.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="I=0" display="inline"><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S2.p7.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="I=\langle 0\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mn>0</mn><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math> is principal.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.p8" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Otherwise, let <math id="Ch2.S2.p8.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S=\left\{{\delta(i)\mid 0\neq i\in I}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>S</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>i</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><mn>0</mn><mo>≠</mo><mi>i</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, non-empty, and pick <math id="Ch2.S2.p8.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="d=\operatorname{argmin}S" display="inline"><mrow><mi>d</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>argmin</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>S</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
Writing <math id="Ch2.S2.p8.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="i=dq+r" display="inline"><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>d</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>q</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mi>r</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, we know <math id="Ch2.S2.p8.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="r=i-dq\in I" display="inline"><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>−</mo><mrow><mi>d</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>q</mi></mrow></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow></math>.
But, since <math id="Ch2.S2.p8.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\delta(r)&lt;\delta(d)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>r</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>&lt;</mo><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>d</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S2.p8.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\delta(r)\not\in S" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>r</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>∉</mo><mi>S</mi></mrow></math> and so <math id="Ch2.S2.p8.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="r=0" display="inline"><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>.
Thus, <math id="Ch2.S2.p8.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S\subset\langle d\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mi>S</mi><mo>⊂</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>d</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, and so <math id="Ch2.S2.p8.m9" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S=\langle d\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mi>S</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>d</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math>.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.p9" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">To show that PIDs are UFDs, we need to prove relationships between primes and irreducibles.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem11" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_lemma">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Lemma 2.2.11</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem11.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem11.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p" display="inline"><mi>p</mi></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is prime if and only if <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem11.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R/\langle p\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>p</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math> is a domain.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.p10" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Note that <math id="Ch2.S2.p10.m1" class="ltx_math_unparsed" alttext="p\mid ab\iff(a+\langle p\rangle)(b+\langle p\rangle)=0+\langle p" display="inline"><mrow><mi>p</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0.167em">∣</mo><mi>a</mi><mi>b</mi><mo stretchy="false">⇔</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>a</mi><mo>+</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>p</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>b</mi><mo>+</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>p</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn><mo>+</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>p</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
Thus, <math id="Ch2.S2.p10.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p" display="inline"><mi>p</mi></math> prime if and only if one of the terms is zero, the defining property of a domain.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem12" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_lemma">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Lemma 2.2.12</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem12.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">In <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem12.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R" display="inline"><mi>R</mi></math> PID, and <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem12.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c" display="inline"><mi>c</mi></math> is irreducible, then <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem12.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R/\langle c\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math> is a field (and domain).</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.p11" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">If <math id="Ch2.S2.p11.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle c\rangle=R" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S2.p11.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R/\langle c\rangle=0" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>, a field.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.p12" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Otherwise, consider any non-zero element <math id="Ch2.S2.p12.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a+\langle c\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>+</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, i.e. <math id="Ch2.S2.p12.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a\not\in\langle c\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>∉</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math>.
Now, let <math id="Ch2.S2.p12.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle a\rangle+\langle c\rangle=\langle b\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>a</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>b</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, since we are in a PID.
Since <math id="Ch2.S2.p12.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="0=0a\in\langle a\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mn>0</mn><mo>=</mo><mrow><mn>0</mn><mo>⁢</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>a</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S2.p12.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle c\rangle\subset\langle b\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>⊂</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>b</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, so write <math id="Ch2.S2.p12.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c=bx" display="inline"><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
Moreover, <math id="Ch2.S2.p12.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x" display="inline"><mi>x</mi></math> is not a unit, since <math id="Ch2.S2.p12.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a\in\langle b\rangle\setminus\langle c\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>b</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>∖</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math> (i.e. ideals are not the same), so <math id="Ch2.S2.p12.m9" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b" display="inline"><mi>b</mi></math> is a unit.
Thus, <math id="Ch2.S2.p12.m10" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle b\rangle=R" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>b</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow></math>, with <math id="Ch2.S2.p12.m11" class="ltx_Math" alttext="r=(rb^{-1})b\in\langle b\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msup><mi>b</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>b</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math>.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem13" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 2.2.13</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem13.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">In a PID, then irreducibles are equivalent to primes.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.p13" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">If <math id="Ch2.S2.p13.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c" display="inline"><mi>c</mi></math> irreducible, then <math id="Ch2.S2.p13.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R/\langle c\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math> is a domain, so <math id="Ch2.S2.p13.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c" display="inline"><mi>c</mi></math> prime.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.p14" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">If <math id="Ch2.S2.p14.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c" display="inline"><mi>c</mi></math> prime, and if <math id="Ch2.S2.p14.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c=ab" display="inline"><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, then suppose <math id="Ch2.S2.p14.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c\mid a" display="inline"><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>∣</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow></math>.
Then, <math id="Ch2.S2.p14.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a=cq" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>q</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, <math id="Ch2.S2.p14.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c=cqb" display="inline"><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>q</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch2.S2.p14.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="qb=1" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>q</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></math>, i.e. <math id="Ch2.S2.p14.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b" display="inline"><mi>b</mi></math> is a unit.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem14" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 2.2.14</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem14.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">PIDs are UFDs.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.p15" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">First, we show existence of a factorization, via the algorithm</p>
<ol id="Ch2.S2.I1" class="ltx_enumerate">
<li id="Ch2.S2.I1.i1" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">1.</span> 
<div id="Ch2.S2.I1.i1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">If <math id="Ch2.S2.I1.i1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="r" display="inline"><mi>r</mi></math> irreducible, stop.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li id="Ch2.S2.I1.i2" class="ltx_item" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">2.</span> 
<div id="Ch2.S2.I1.i2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Otherwise, <math id="Ch2.S2.I1.i2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="r=ab" display="inline"><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, both not units, and recurse.</p>
</div>
</li>
</ol>
<p class="ltx_p">For any path <math id="Ch2.S2.p15.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a_{1}\ldots" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>a</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi></mrow></math> we get an ascending chain of ideals <math id="Ch2.S2.p15.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle a_{1}\rangle\subset\ldots" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msub><mi>a</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>⊂</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi></mrow></math>.
Considering <math id="Ch2.S2.p15.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="J=\cap\langle a_{i}\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo rspace="0.1389em">=</mo><mrow><mo lspace="0.1389em" rspace="0em">∩</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msub><mi>a</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math> is an ideal, then <math id="Ch2.S2.p15.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="J=\langle a_{n}\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msub><mi>a</mi><mi>n</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, i.e. the stopping point.
Thus, the algorithm terminates.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.p16" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Arguing uniqueness, we induct on <math id="Ch2.S2.p16.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\max(n,m)" display="inline"><mrow><mi>max</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>n</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></math>.
Since <math id="Ch2.S2.p16.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p_{1}\mid a" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>p</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>∣</mo><mi>a</mi></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S2.p16.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p_{1}\mid q_{i}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>p</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>∣</mo><msub><mi>q</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></mrow></math>, say <math id="Ch2.S2.p16.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="q_{1}" display="inline"><msub><mi>q</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></math>.
Then, <math id="Ch2.S2.p16.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="p_{1}" display="inline"><msub><mi>p</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></math> and <math id="Ch2.S2.p16.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="q_{1}" display="inline"><msub><mi>q</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></math> are associates (since both irreducible), so inducting on <math id="Ch2.S2.p16.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a^{\prime}=v^{\prime}q_{2}\cdots q_{m}=u^{\prime}p_{2}\cdots p_{m}" display="inline"><mrow><msup><mi>a</mi><mo>′</mo></msup><mo>=</mo><mrow><msup><mi>v</mi><mo>′</mo></msup><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>q</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">⋯</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>q</mi><mi>m</mi></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msup><mi>u</mi><mo>′</mo></msup><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>p</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">⋯</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>p</mi><mi>m</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></math>, we win.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.p17" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We conclude this section with two examples of Euclidean domains, which we proved are also UFDs.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem15" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_example">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Example 2.2.15</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem15.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">Let <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem15.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbb{Z}[i]=\left\{{a+bi\mid a,b\in\mathbb{Z}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>ℤ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mi>i</mi><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>i</mi></mrow></mrow><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, and define <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem15.p1.m2" class="ltx_math_unparsed" alttext="\delta(z)=\left|\bigr{.}z\right|^{2}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>z</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0em">=</mo><mo fence="false">|</mo><mo lspace="0.167em" mathsize="1.200em" rspace="0.167em">.</mo><mi>z</mi><msup><mo fence="false">|</mo><mn>2</mn></msup></mrow></math>.
Note that <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem15.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\delta(zw)=\delta(z)\delta(w)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>w</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>z</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>w</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.
For any <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem15.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a,b\in\mathbb{Z}[i]" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mi>ℤ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mi>i</mi><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, with <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem15.p1.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b\neq 0" display="inline"><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>≠</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>, we need to show that <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem15.p1.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a=bq+r" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>q</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mi>r</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, with <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem15.p1.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\delta(r)&lt;\delta(g)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>r</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>&lt;</mo><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem15.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">For any <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem15.p2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="z\in\mathbb{C}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>ℂ</mi></mrow></math>, we can find <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem15.p2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="q\in\mathbb{Z}[i]" display="inline"><mrow><mi>q</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mi>ℤ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mi>i</mi><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math> where <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem15.p2.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\delta(z-c)&lt;(1/2)^{2}+(1/2)^{2}=1/2" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo>−</mo><mi>c</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>&lt;</mo><mrow><msup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>/</mo><mn>2</mn></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mn>2</mn></msup><mo>+</mo><msup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>/</mo><mn>2</mn></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mn>2</mn></msup></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>/</mo><mn>2</mn></mrow></mrow></math>, by choosing the closest lattice point.
Thus, choosing <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem15.p2.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="q\in\mathbb{Z}[i]" display="inline"><mrow><mi>q</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mi>ℤ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mi>i</mi><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math> the closest point to <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem15.p2.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a/b" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></math>, and <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem15.p2.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="r=a-qb" display="inline"><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>−</mo><mrow><mi>q</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, we win.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_example">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Example 2.2.16</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">Consider <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="F[x]" display="inline"><mrow><mi>F</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, the (finite degree) polynomials over a field <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="F" display="inline"><mi>F</mi></math>, and the function <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\delta(f)=\deg f" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>f</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>deg</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>f</mi></mrow></mrow></math> (with <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\delta(0)=-\infty" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>0</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>−</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">∞</mi></mrow></mrow></math>).
Note that <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16.p1.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\delta(fg)=\delta(f)+\delta(g)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>f</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.
For any <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16.p1.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f,g\in F[x]" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mi>F</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math> with <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16.p1.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="m=\delta g\geq 0" display="inline"><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow><mo>≥</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>, we need to show <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16.p1.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f=gq+r" display="inline"><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>q</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mi>r</mi></mrow></mrow></math> with <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16.p1.m9" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\delta(r)&lt;\delta(g)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>r</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>&lt;</mo><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">Inducting on <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16.p2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n=\delta(f)" display="inline"><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>f</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, if <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16.p2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\delta(f)&lt;\delta(g)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>f</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>&lt;</mo><mrow><mi>δ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>g</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16.p2.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f=g0+r" display="inline"><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><mo>+</mo><mi>r</mi></mrow></mrow></math> wins.
Otherwise, write <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16.p2.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f^{\prime}=f-(f_{n}g_{m}^{-1})x^{n-m}g" display="inline"><mrow><msup><mi>f</mi><mo>′</mo></msup><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>−</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>f</mi><mi>n</mi></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msubsup><mi>g</mi><mi>m</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msubsup></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><msup><mi>x</mi><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>−</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow></msup><mo>⁢</mo><mi>g</mi></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, and inducting, <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16.p2.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f^{\prime}=gq^{\prime}+r" display="inline"><mrow><msup><mi>f</mi><mo>′</mo></msup><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msup><mi>q</mi><mo>′</mo></msup></mrow><mo>+</mo><mi>r</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
Now, <math id="Ch2.S2.Thmtheorem16.p2.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f=g(q^{\prime}+f_{n}g_{m}^{-1}x^{n-m})+r" display="inline"><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>g</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msup><mi>q</mi><mo>′</mo></msup><mo>+</mo><mrow><msub><mi>f</mi><mi>n</mi></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msubsup><mi>g</mi><mi>m</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msubsup><mo>⁢</mo><msup><mi>x</mi><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>−</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow></msup></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>+</mo><mi>r</mi></mrow></mrow></math> wins.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
</section>
<section id="Ch2.S3" class="ltx_section">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">2.3 </span>Chinese Remainder Theorem</h3>

<div id="Ch2.S3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">First, we prove the first isomorphism theorem for rings.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem1" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 2.3.1</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f:R\to S" display="inline"><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mi>S</mi></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is a ring homomorphism if it is a group homomorphism with <math id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem1.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f(rs)=f(r)f(s)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>s</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>r</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>s</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem2" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 2.3.2</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">If <math id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f:R\to S" display="inline"><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mi>S</mi></mrow></mrow></math> is a surjective ring homomorphism, then <math id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem2.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R/\ker f\cong S" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><mrow><mi>ker</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>f</mi></mrow></mrow><mo>≅</mo><mi>S</mi></mrow></math></span></p>
</div>
</div>
