<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S3.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We know that they are isomorphic as groups, with <math id="Ch2.S3.p2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\pi:(r+K)\mapsto f(r)" display="inline"><mrow><mi>π</mi><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>K</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo stretchy="false">↦</mo><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>r</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow></math> the group isomorphism.
Moreover, it is also a ring isomorphism: <math id="Ch2.S3.p2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\pi((r+\ker f)(s+\ker f))=\pi(rs+\ker f)=rs=\pi(r+\ker f)\pi(s+\ker f)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>π</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>ker</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>f</mi></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>s</mi><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>ker</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>f</mi></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>π</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>s</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>ker</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>f</mi></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>s</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>π</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>ker</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>f</mi></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>π</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>s</mi><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>ker</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>f</mi></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S3.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Now, we are ready for the Chinese Remainder Theorem.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem3" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 2.3.3</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">Let <math id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem3.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="I_{1},\ldots,I_{k}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow></math> be ideals s.t. <math id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem3.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="I_{i}+I_{j}=R" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>I</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mi>j</mi></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow></math> for all pairs <math id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem3.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="1\leq i,j\leq k" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>≤</mo><mi>i</mi></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mi>j</mi><mo>≤</mo><mi>k</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
Then,</span></p>
<table id="Ch2.Ex4" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_center"><math id="Ch2.Ex4.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R/(I_{1}\cdots I_{k})\cong(R/I_{1})\times\cdots\times(R/I_{k})" display="block"><mrow><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">⋯</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>≅</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo rspace="0.055em" stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">⋯</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem4" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_lemma">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Lemma 2.3.4</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem4.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">If <math id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem4.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="I_{1}+I_{2}=R" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem4.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="I_{1}I_{2}=I_{1}\cap I_{2}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>∩</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S3.p4" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We know <math id="Ch2.S3.p4.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="I_{1}I_{2}\subset I_{1}\cap I_{2}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo>⊂</mo><mrow><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>∩</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow></mrow></math>.
Moreover, letting <math id="Ch2.S3.p4.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="i_{1}+i_{2}=1" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></math>, then for any <math id="Ch2.S3.p4.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="i\in I_{1}\cap I_{2}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>∩</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch2.S3.p4.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="i=i(i_{1}+ii_{2})\in I_{1}I_{2}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow></mrow></math>.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">CRT.</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S3.p5" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">If <math id="Ch2.S3.p5.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="k=1" display="inline"><mrow><mi>k</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></math>, then the statement is trivial.
For <math id="Ch2.S3.p5.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="k=2" display="inline"><mrow><mi>k</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>2</mn></mrow></math>, consider the homomorphism</p>
<table id="Ch2.Ex5" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_center"><math id="Ch2.Ex5.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f:R\to R/I_{1}\times R/I_{2}\qquad r\mapsto(r+I_{1},r+I_{2})" display="block"><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow><mo>/</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow></mrow><mspace width="2em"></mspace><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo stretchy="false">↦</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S3.p6" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Let <math id="Ch2.S3.p6.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="i_{1}+i_{2}=1" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></math>, for <math id="Ch2.S3.p6.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="i_{j}\in I_{j}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>i</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>∈</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mi>j</mi></msub></mrow></math>.
For any <math id="Ch2.S3.p6.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(y_{1}+I_{1},y_{2}+I_{2})" display="inline"><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>y</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><msub><mi>y</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></math>, consider <math id="Ch2.S3.p6.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x=i_{1}y_{2}+i_{2}y_{1}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>y</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>y</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, so</p>
<table id="Ch3.S3.EGx2" class="ltx_equationgroup ltx_eqn_align ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody id="Ch2.Ex6"><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_right ltx_eqn_cell"><math id="Ch2.Ex6.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\displaystyle f(x)" display="inline"><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></math></td>
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_left ltx_eqn_cell"><math id="Ch2.Ex6.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\displaystyle=((i_{1}y_{2}+i_{2}y_{1})+I_{1},(i_{1}y_{2}+i_{2}y_{1})+I_{2})" display="inline"><mrow><mi></mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>y</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>y</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>y</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>y</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
</tr></tbody>
<tbody id="Ch2.Ex7"><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_td ltx_eqn_cell"></td>
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_left ltx_eqn_cell"><math id="Ch2.Ex7.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\displaystyle=(i_{1}y_{2}+(1-i_{1})y_{1}+I_{1},(1-i_{2})y_{2}+i_{2}y_{1}+I_{2})" display="inline"><mrow><mi></mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>y</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>y</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>y</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><msub><mi>i</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>y</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
</tr></tbody>
<tbody id="Ch2.Ex8"><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_td ltx_eqn_cell"></td>
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_left ltx_eqn_cell"><math id="Ch2.Ex8.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\displaystyle=(y_{1}+I_{1},y_{2}+I_{2})" display="inline"><mrow><mi></mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>y</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><msub><mi>y</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p class="ltx_p">and <math id="Ch2.S3.p6.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f" display="inline"><mi>f</mi></math> is surjective.
Moreover, <math id="Ch2.S3.p6.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\ker f=\left\{{r\mid r+I_{1}=I_{1},r+I_{2}=I_{2}}\right\}=I_{1}\cap I_{2}=I_{1%
}I_{2}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>ker</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>f</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mi>r</mi><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>∩</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow></mrow></math>, so we win.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S3.p7" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Finally, for <math id="Ch2.S3.p7.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="k&gt;2" display="inline"><mrow><mi>k</mi><mo>&gt;</mo><mn>2</mn></mrow></math>, let <math id="Ch2.S3.p7.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="J=I_{1}\cdots I_{k-1}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">⋯</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mrow><mi>k</mi><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msub></mrow></mrow></math>.
Consider <math id="Ch2.S3.p7.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a_{j}+b_{j}=1" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>a</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>b</mi><mi>j</mi></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></math>, for <math id="Ch2.S3.p7.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a_{j}\in I_{j}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>a</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>∈</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mi>j</mi></msub></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch2.S3.p7.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b_{j}\in I_{k}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>b</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>∈</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow></math>, for <math id="Ch2.S3.p7.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="1\leq j&lt;k" display="inline"><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>≤</mo><mi>j</mi><mo>&lt;</mo><mi>k</mi></mrow></math>.
Then, we can invoke the induction hypothesis, since <math id="Ch2.S3.p7.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="1=\prod(a_{j}+b_{j})\in J+I_{k}" display="inline"><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo rspace="0.111em">=</mo><mrow><mo rspace="0em">∏</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>a</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>b</mi><mi>j</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></math>, so <math id="Ch2.S3.p7.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="J+I_{k}=R" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>J</mi><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow></math>.
Now,</p>
<table id="Ch2.Ex9" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_center"><math id="Ch2.Ex9.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R/(I_{1}\cdots I_{k})=R/JI_{k}\cong R/J\times R/I_{k}\cong(R/I_{1}\times\cdots
R%
/I_{k-1})\times R/I_{k}" display="block"><mrow><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">⋯</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>J</mi></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow><mo>≅</mo><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>J</mi></mrow><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow><mo>/</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow><mo>≅</mo><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">⋯</mi></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow><mo>/</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mrow><mi>k</mi><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msub></mrow><mo rspace="0.055em" stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow><mo>/</mo><msub><mi>I</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p class="ltx_p">∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S3.p8" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We study the implications on PIDs.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem5" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_lemma">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Lemma 2.3.5</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem5.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">For <math id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem5.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a,b" display="inline"><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>b</mi></mrow></math> distinct (not associates) irreducibles in <math id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem5.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R" display="inline"><mi>R</mi></math> a PID, then <math id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem5.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle a^{n}\rangle+\langle b^{m}\rangle=R" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msup><mi>a</mi><mi>n</mi></msup><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msup><mi>b</mi><mi>m</mi></msup><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow></math>, for <math id="Ch2.S3.Thmtheorem5.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n,m\geq 0" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo>≥</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch2.S3.p9" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Let <math id="Ch2.S3.p9.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle a^{n}\rangle+\langle b^{m}\rangle=\langle c\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msup><mi>a</mi><mi>n</mi></msup><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msup><mi>b</mi><mi>m</mi></msup><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math>.
Then, <math id="Ch2.S3.p9.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a^{n}\in\langle c\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><msup><mi>a</mi><mi>n</mi></msup><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math> so <math id="Ch2.S3.p9.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a^{n}=cx" display="inline"><mrow><msup><mi>a</mi><mi>n</mi></msup><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.
Similarly, <math id="Ch2.S3.p9.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b^{m}=cy" display="inline"><mrow><msup><mi>b</mi><mi>m</mi></msup><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>y</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S3.p10" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">By UFD properties, then <math id="Ch2.S3.p10.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c=ua^{i}=vb^{j}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>u</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msup><mi>a</mi><mi>i</mi></msup></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>v</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msup><mi>b</mi><mi>j</mi></msup></mrow></mrow></math>, for <math id="Ch2.S3.p10.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="i\leq n" display="inline"><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>≤</mo><mi>n</mi></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch2.S3.p10.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b\leq j" display="inline"><mrow><mi>b</mi><mo>≤</mo><mi>j</mi></mrow></math>, <math id="Ch2.S3.p10.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="u" display="inline"><mi>u</mi></math> and <math id="Ch2.S3.p10.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="v" display="inline"><mi>v</mi></math> units.
But, since <math id="Ch2.S3.p10.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a" display="inline"><mi>a</mi></math> and <math id="Ch2.S3.p10.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="b" display="inline"><mi>b</mi></math> are not associates, then <math id="Ch2.S3.p10.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="i=j=0" display="inline"><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>j</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>, and <math id="Ch2.S3.p10.m9" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c" display="inline"><mi>c</mi></math> is a unit and <math id="Ch2.S3.p10.m10" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle c\rangle=R" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow></math>.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch2.S3.p11" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">For example,</p>
<table id="Ch2.Ex10" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_center"><math id="Ch2.Ex10.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="Z_{12}=\mathbb{Z}/\langle 12\rangle=\mathbb{Z}/(\langle 3\rangle\langle 4%
\rangle)=\mathbb{Z}/\langle 3\rangle\times\mathbb{Z}/\langle 4\rangle=Z_{3}%
\times Z_{4}" display="block"><mrow><msub><mi>Z</mi><mn>12</mn></msub><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>ℤ</mi><mo>/</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mn>12</mn><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>ℤ</mi><mo>/</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mn>3</mn><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mn>4</mn><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>ℤ</mi><mo>/</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mn>3</mn><mo rspace="0.055em" stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>ℤ</mi></mrow><mo>/</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mn>4</mn><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mi>Z</mi><mn>3</mn></msub><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><msub><mi>Z</mi><mn>4</mn></msub></mrow></mrow></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p class="ltx_p">so that given <math id="Ch2.S3.p11.m1" class="ltx_math_unparsed" alttext="\llbracket a\rrbracket_{3}" display="inline"><msub><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟦</mo><mi>a</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟧</mo></mrow><mn>3</mn></msub></math> and <math id="Ch2.S3.p11.m2" class="ltx_math_unparsed" alttext="\llbracket a\rrbracket_{4}" display="inline"><msub><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟦</mo><mi>a</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟧</mo></mrow><mn>4</mn></msub></math>, we can find <math id="Ch2.S3.p11.m3" class="ltx_math_unparsed" alttext="\llbracket a\rrbracket_{12}" display="inline"><msub><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟦</mo><mi>a</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟧</mo></mrow><mn>12</mn></msub></math> uniquely.
In general, we can factor <math id="Ch2.S3.p11.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a" display="inline"><mi>a</mi></math> into distinct irreducibles.</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section id="Ch3" class="ltx_chapter">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_chapter">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_chapter">Chapter 3 </span>Module Theory</h2>

<section id="Ch3.S1" class="ltx_section">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">3.1 </span>Modules</h3>

<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem1" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 3.1.1</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">A <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R" display="inline"><mi>R</mi></math>-module <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem1.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math> is an abelian group <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem1.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(M,0,+)" display="inline"><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>M</mi><mo>,</mo><mn>0</mn><mo rspace="0em">,</mo><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">+</mo><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></math> with an operation <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem1.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R\times M\to M" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></math> where</span></p>
<table id="Ch3.Ex1" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_center"><math id="Ch3.Ex1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(r_{1}+r_{2})m=r_{1}m+r_{2}m\qquad r(m_{1}+m_{2})=rm_{1}+rm_{2}\qquad r_{1}(r_%
{2}m)=(r_{1}r_{2})m\qquad 1_{R}m=m" display="block"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>r</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow></mrow></mrow><mspace width="2em"></mspace><mrow><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>m</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>m</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>m</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>m</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow></mrow></mrow><mspace width="2em"></mspace><mrow><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>r</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow></mrow><mspace width="2em"></mspace><mrow><mrow><msub><mn>1</mn><mi>R</mi></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem2" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 3.1.2</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N\triangleleft M" display="inline"><mrow><mi>N</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⊲</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is a submodule if <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem2.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="rn\in N" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>n</mi></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We can think of modules as groups that are acted on by rings.
Or, we can think of modules as vector spaces on rings.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem3" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_example">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Example 3.1.3</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem3.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R" display="inline"><mi>R</mi></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is an <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem3.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R" display="inline"><mi>R</mi></math>-module, with the normal multiplication.
Submodules are ideals.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem4" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 3.1.4</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem4.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem4.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f:M\to N" display="inline"><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is a module homomorphism if it is a group homorphism where <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem4.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f(rm)=rf(m)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem5" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 3.1.5</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem5.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem5.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M/N" display="inline"><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> quotient group is a quotient module with operation <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem5.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="r(m+N)=rm+N" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem6" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 3.1.6</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem6.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem6.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f:M\to N" display="inline"><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> surjective, then <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem6.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M/\ker f\cong N" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo>/</mo><mrow><mi>ker</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>f</mi></mrow></mrow><mo>≅</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S1.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">They are isomorphic as groups, with <math id="Ch3.S1.p2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\pi(m+K)=f(m)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>π</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>K</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.
Moreover, it is a module homomorphism,</p>
<table id="Ch3.Ex2" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_center"><math id="Ch3.Ex2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\pi(r(m+K))=\pi(rm+K)=f(rm)=rf(m)=r\pi(m+K)" display="block"><mrow><mrow><mi>π</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>K</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>π</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mi>K</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>f</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>π</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>K</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p class="ltx_p">∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S1.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Moreover, we have all our familiar linear algebra concepts.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem7" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 3.1.7</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem7.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem7.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S\subset M" display="inline"><mrow><mi>S</mi><mo>⊂</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">, then the span of <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem7.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline"><mi>S</mi></math>, <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem7.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle S\rangle=\left\{{\sum r_{i}s_{i}\mid r_{i}\in R,s_{i}\in S}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>S</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><mo lspace="0em">∑</mo><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>s</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></mrow></mrow><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>∈</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><msub><mi>s</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>∈</mo><mi>S</mi></mrow></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem8" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 3.1.8</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem8.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem8.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline"><mi>S</mi></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> generates <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem8.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math> if <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem8.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle S\rangle=M" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>S</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem9" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 3.1.9</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem9.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem9.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline"><mi>S</mi></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is linearly independent if <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem9.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sum r_{i}s_{i}=0\implies r_{i}=0" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo>∑</mo><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>s</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn><mo stretchy="false">⟹</mo><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem10" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 3.1.10</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem10.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S" display="inline"><mi>S</mi></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is a basis if it is a linearly independent generator.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S1.p4" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">With this, we note some basic properties of modules.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem11" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_lemma">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Lemma 3.1.11</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem11.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem11.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M\cong R^{n}/N" display="inline"><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo>≅</mo><mrow><msup><mi>R</mi><mi>n</mi></msup><mo>/</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">, for some <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem11.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N\triangleleft M" display="inline"><mrow><mi>N</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⊲</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S1.p5" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Let <math id="Ch3.S1.p5.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math> be generated by <math id="Ch3.S1.p5.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left\{{x_{1},\ldots,x_{m}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mo>{</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>m</mi></msub><mo>}</mo></mrow></math>.
Consider <math id="Ch3.S1.p5.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="f:R^{n}\to M" display="inline"><mrow><mi>f</mi><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><msup><mi>R</mi><mi>n</mi></msup><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow></math> by <math id="Ch3.S1.p5.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(r_{1},\ldots,r_{m})\to\sum r_{i}x_{i}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>r</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>m</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0.111em" stretchy="false">→</mo><mrow><mo>∑</mo><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, surjective homomorphism.
Then, <math id="Ch3.S1.p5.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\ker f" display="inline"><mrow><mi>ker</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>f</mi></mrow></math> is an submodule, and so we win.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S1.p6" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">In particular, if <math id="Ch3.S1.p6.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math> is cyclic, i.e. generated by one element, then <math id="Ch3.S1.p6.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M\cong R/I" display="inline"><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo>≅</mo><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow></mrow></math> and we can think of it as a ring.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S1.p7" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Finally, we reintroduce the direct sum.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem12" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 3.1.12</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem12.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">Then, <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem12.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N_{1}\oplus\ldots\oplus N_{k}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>N</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⊕</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>⊕</mo><msub><mi>N</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow></math> is a module over the group <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem12.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N_{1}\times\ldots\times N_{k}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>N</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">×</mo><msub><mi>N</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow></math>, <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem12.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="r(n_{1},\ldots,n_{k})\mapsto(rn_{1},\ldots,rn_{k})" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>n</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>n</mi><mi>k</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">↦</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>n</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>n</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></math></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem13" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_lemma">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Lemma 3.1.13</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem13.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">Let <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem13.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N_{1},\ldots,N_{k}\triangleleft M" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>N</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><mrow><msub><mi>N</mi><mi>k</mi></msub><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⊲</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, where <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem13.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle\cup_{1\leq i\leq k}N_{i}\rangle=M" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mrow><msub><mo lspace="0em">∪</mo><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>≤</mo><mi>i</mi><mo>≤</mo><mi>k</mi></mrow></msub><msub><mi>N</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></math>, and <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem13.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N_{j}\cap(\langle\cup_{i\neq j}N_{i}\rangle)=0" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>N</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>∩</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mrow><msub><mo lspace="0em">∪</mo><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>≠</mo><mi>j</mi></mrow></msub><msub><mi>N</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>.
Then, <math id="Ch3.S1.Thmtheorem13.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N_{1}\oplus\ldots N_{k}\cong M" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>N</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⊕</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>N</mi><mi>k</mi></msub></mrow></mrow><mo>≅</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S1.p8" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Consider the map <math id="Ch3.S1.p8.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(n_{1},\ldots,n_{k})\mapsto\sum n_{i}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>n</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>n</mi><mi>k</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0.111em" stretchy="false">↦</mo><mrow><mo>∑</mo><msub><mi>n</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></math>.
Then, it is surjective, since <math id="Ch3.S1.p8.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle\cup_{1\leq i\leq k}N_{i}\rangle=M" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mrow><msub><mo lspace="0em">∪</mo><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>≤</mo><mi>i</mi><mo>≤</mo><mi>k</mi></mrow></msub><msub><mi>N</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></math>.
Moreover, it is injective, since if <math id="Ch3.S1.p8.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sum n_{i}=0" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo>∑</mo><msub><mi>n</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch3.S1.p8.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n_{i}=\sum_{i\neq j}-n_{j}\in N_{i}\cap(\langle\cup_{i\neq j}N_{j}\rangle)=0" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>n</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo rspace="0.111em">=</mo><mrow><msub><mo rspace="0em">∑</mo><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>≠</mo><mi>j</mi></mrow></msub><mo lspace="0em">−</mo><msub><mi>n</mi><mi>j</mi></msub></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><msub><mi>N</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>∩</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mrow><msub><mo lspace="0em">∪</mo><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>≠</mo><mi>j</mi></mrow></msub><msub><mi>N</mi><mi>j</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
</section>
<section id="Ch3.S2" class="ltx_section">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">3.2 </span>Bases and Dimension</h3>

<div id="Ch3.S2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Modules without bases are easy to construct.
For example, consider <math id="Ch3.S2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbb{Z}_{n}" display="inline"><msub><mi>ℤ</mi><mi>n</mi></msub></math> as a <math id="Ch3.S2.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\mathbb{Z}" display="inline"><mi>ℤ</mi></math>-module, where since <math id="Ch3.S2.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="nx=0" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>x</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>, then there are no linearly independent sets.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem1" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 3.2.1</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is free if it has a basis.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem2" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 3.2.2</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem2.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem2.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="m\in M" display="inline"><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is torsion if <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem2.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="rm=0" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math> for <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem2.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="r\neq 0" display="inline"><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>≠</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>.
<math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem2.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M^{\text{tors}}=\left\{{m\mid m\text{ torsion}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><msup><mi>M</mi><mtext class="ltx_mathvariant_italic">tors</mtext></msup><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mi>m</mi><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mtext class="ltx_mathvariant_italic"> torsion</mtext></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, and say <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem2.p1.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math> is torsion if <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem2.p1.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M=M^{\text{tors}}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo>=</mo><msup><mi>M</mi><mtext class="ltx_mathvariant_italic">tors</mtext></msup></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem3" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 3.2.3</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">If <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem3.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math> is free, then <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem3.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\dim M" display="inline"><mrow><mo rspace="0.167em">dim</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></math> is the size of a basis.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem4" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_lemma">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Lemma 3.2.4</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem4.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">In a domain, <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem4.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M^{\text{tors}}\triangleleft M" display="inline"><mrow><msup><mi>M</mi><mtext class="ltx_mathvariant_italic">tors</mtext></msup><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⊲</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></math></span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S2.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">It is a subgroup, since for <math id="Ch3.S2.p2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="m,n" display="inline"><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>,</mo><mi>n</mi></mrow></math> torsion with <math id="Ch3.S2.p2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="rm=sn=0" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>s</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>n</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch3.S2.p2.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="rs(m-n)=0" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>s</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>−</mo><mi>n</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math> where <math id="Ch3.S2.p2.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="rs\neq 0" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>s</mi></mrow><mo>≠</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>.
Moreover, for any <math id="Ch3.S2.p2.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x\in R" display="inline"><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow></math>, <math id="Ch3.S2.p2.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="r(xm)=x(rm)=0" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>, so <math id="Ch3.S2.p2.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="xm" display="inline"><mrow><mi>x</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow></math> also torison.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.p3" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">If <math id="Ch3.S2.p3.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M^{\text{tors}}\neq 0" display="inline"><mrow><msup><mi>M</mi><mtext>tors</mtext></msup><mo>≠</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch3.S2.p3.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math> is not free.
Similarly, if <math id="Ch3.S2.p3.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math> is free, then <math id="Ch3.S2.p3.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M^{\text{tors}}=0" display="inline"><mrow><msup><mi>M</mi><mtext>tors</mtext></msup><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>.
Later, we will show that every module <math id="Ch3.S2.p3.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math> is uniquely decomposed into a torsion and free part, but now we focus on studying the free component, in particular proving that dimension is well-defined.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.p4" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We reduce the question to vector spaces.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem5" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 3.2.5</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem5.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem5.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="I" display="inline"><mi>I</mi></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> ideal, then <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem5.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="IM=\left\{{im\mid i\in I,m\in M}\right\}\triangleleft M" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo fence="true" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∣</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>∈</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⊲</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem6" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_definition">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Definition 3.2.6</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem6.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem6.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M/IM" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> is an <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem6.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R/I" display="inline"><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow></math> module, with <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem6.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(r+I)(m+IM)\mapsto rm+IM" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">↦</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>r</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem7" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 3.2.7</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem7.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem7.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> free, then <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem7.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M/IM" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></math> is free, with same sized bases.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S2.p5" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Let <math id="Ch3.S2.p5.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S=\left\{{x_{1},\ldots,x_{m}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>S</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>m</mi></msub><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math> be a basis of <math id="Ch3.S2.p5.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math>, and consider <math id="Ch3.S2.p5.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S^{\prime}=\left\{{x_{i}+IM}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><msup><mi>S</mi><mo>′</mo></msup><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></math>.
First, note that <math id="Ch3.S2.p5.m4" class="ltx_math_unparsed" alttext="IM=\langle\left\{{i_{j}x_{j}\mid i_{j}\in I}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>I</mi><mi>M</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mrow><mo>{</mo><msub><mi>i</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0.167em">∣</mo><msub><mi>i</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>∈</mo><mi>I</mi><mo>}</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.p6" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Now, for any <math id="Ch3.S2.p6.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="m+IM\in M/IM" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow><mo>∈</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, writing <math id="Ch3.S2.p6.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="m=\sum r_{j}x_{j}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo rspace="0.111em">=</mo><mrow><mo>∑</mo><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>j</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch3.S2.p6.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="m+IM=\sum(r_{j}+I)(x_{j}+IM)" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow><mo rspace="0.111em">=</mo><mrow><mo rspace="0em">∑</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, so <math id="Ch3.S2.p6.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="S^{\prime}" display="inline"><msup><mi>S</mi><mo>′</mo></msup></math> is generating.
Moreover, if <math id="Ch3.S2.p6.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sum(r_{j}+I)(x_{j}+IM)=im+IM=0" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo rspace="0em">∑</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>, where <math id="Ch3.S2.p6.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="im=\sum i_{j}x_{j}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><mo rspace="0.111em">=</mo><mrow><mo>∑</mo><mrow><msub><mi>i</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>j</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch3.S2.p6.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\sum(r_{j}-i_{j})x_{j}=0" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo rspace="0em">∑</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>−</mo><msub><mi>i</mi><mi>j</mi></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>j</mi></msub></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>, and because <math id="Ch3.S2.p6.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="x_{j}" display="inline"><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>j</mi></msub></math> are independent, <math id="Ch3.S2.p6.m9" class="ltx_Math" alttext="r_{j}+I=I" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow></math>.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.p7" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">In a PID, we can choose an irreducible <math id="Ch3.S2.p7.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="c" display="inline"><mi>c</mi></math> and let <math id="Ch3.S2.p7.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="I=\langle c\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math>, so that <math id="Ch3.S2.p7.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R/I" display="inline"><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow></math> is a field.
In general, we can always choose an ideal (say, “maximal”) where <math id="Ch3.S2.p7.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R/I" display="inline"><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow></math> is a field, but proof omitted here (requires axiom of choice).</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem8" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 3.2.8</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem8.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem8.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic"> free <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem8.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R" display="inline"><mi>R</mi></math>-module, then <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem8.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\dim M" display="inline"><mrow><mo rspace="0.167em">dim</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></math> is well-defined.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S2.p8" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Consider any two bases <math id="Ch3.S2.p8.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left\{{x_{i}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mo>{</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>}</mo></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch3.S2.p8.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left\{{y_{i}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mo>{</mo><msub><mi>y</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>}</mo></mrow></math> of <math id="Ch3.S2.p8.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math>.
Then, <math id="Ch3.S2.p8.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left\{{x_{i}+IM}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch3.S2.p8.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left\{{y_{i}+IM}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><msub><mi>y</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></math> are bases of <math id="Ch3.S2.p8.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M/IM" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></math>, which is a vector space.
But, in a vector space, <math id="Ch3.S2.p8.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\dim M/IM" display="inline"><mrow><mo rspace="0.167em">dim</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow></math> is well-defined, so the size of the two bases are the same.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.p9" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Proving that dimension is well-defined in a vector space is easy by considering the change of basis matrix.
It is clearly invertible, and thus applying Gaussian elimination, its reduced row-echelon form is <math id="Ch3.S2.p9.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="I" display="inline"><mi>I</mi></math>, i.e. is square.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem9" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 3.2.9</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem9.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">In a PID, <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem9.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math> free, then <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem9.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N\triangleleft M" display="inline"><mrow><mi>N</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⊲</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></math> is also free, with <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem9.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="n=\dim N\leq\dim M=m" display="inline"><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo rspace="0.1389em">=</mo><mrow><mo lspace="0.1389em" rspace="0.167em">dim</mo><mi>N</mi></mrow><mo rspace="0.1389em">≤</mo><mrow><mo lspace="0.1389em" rspace="0.167em">dim</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow></math>.
Moreover, there exists a basis <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem9.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left\{{a_{1}x_{1},\ldots,a_{n}x_{n}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><msub><mi>a</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><mrow><msub><mi>a</mi><mi>n</mi></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>n</mi></msub></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem9.p1.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left\{{x_{1},\ldots,x_{m}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mo>{</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>m</mi></msub><mo>}</mo></mrow></math> of <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem9.p1.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N" display="inline"><mi>N</mi></math> and <math id="Ch3.S2.Thmtheorem9.p1.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math> respectively.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S2.p10" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">It is enough to prove it for <math id="Ch3.S2.p10.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M=R^{m}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo>=</mo><msup><mi>R</mi><mi>m</mi></msup></mrow></math>.
We induct on <math id="Ch3.S2.p10.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\dim M" display="inline"><mrow><mo rspace="0.167em">dim</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></math>.
For <math id="Ch3.S2.p10.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="m=1" display="inline"><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch3.S2.p10.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N=\langle a_{1}\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mi>N</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msub><mi>a</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math> (since ideal in the ring <math id="Ch3.S2.p10.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R/I" display="inline"><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>I</mi></mrow></math>), and so <math id="Ch3.S2.p10.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N" display="inline"><mi>N</mi></math> free, with <math id="Ch3.S2.p10.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left\{{a_{1}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mo>{</mo><msub><mi>a</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>}</mo></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch3.S2.p10.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left\{{e_{1}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mo>{</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>}</mo></mrow></math> are our bases (or, if <math id="Ch3.S2.p10.m9" class="ltx_Math" alttext="a_{1}=0" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>a</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></math>, then <math id="Ch3.S2.p10.m10" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left\{{}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mo>{</mo><mo>}</mo></mrow></math> is a basis for <math id="Ch3.S2.p10.m11" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N" display="inline"><mi>N</mi></math>).</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.p11" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Otherwise, consider any <math id="Ch3.S2.p11.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\phi:M\to R" display="inline"><mrow><mi>ϕ</mi><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mi>R</mi></mrow></mrow></math> homomorphism.
Then, <math id="Ch3.S2.p11.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\phi(N)" display="inline"><mrow><mi>ϕ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>N</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></math> is an ideal in <math id="Ch3.S2.p11.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="R" display="inline"><mi>R</mi></math>, so <math id="Ch3.S2.p11.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\phi(N)=\langle a_{1}\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>ϕ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>N</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msub><mi>a</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math>.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.p12" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Now, let <math id="Ch3.S2.p12.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left\{{x_{i}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mo>{</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>}</mo></mrow></math> be a basis of <math id="Ch3.S2.p12.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math>, and <math id="Ch3.S2.p12.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left\{{y_{i}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mo>{</mo><msub><mi>y</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>}</mo></mrow></math> homomorphisms with <math id="Ch3.S2.p12.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="y_{i}:x_{j}\mapsto\delta_{ij}" display="inline"><mrow><msub><mi>y</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>j</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">↦</mo><msub><mi>δ</mi><mrow><mi>i</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>j</mi></mrow></msub></mrow></mrow></math>.
For any <math id="Ch3.S2.p12.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="v\in\phi^{-1}(a_{1})" display="inline"><mrow><mi>v</mi><mo>∈</mo><mrow><msup><mi>ϕ</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>a</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, since <math id="Ch3.S2.p12.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\phi(N)\subset\langle a_{1}\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>ϕ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>N</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>⊂</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msub><mi>a</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></math>,</p>
<table id="Ch3.Ex3" class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table">

<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_center"><math id="Ch3.Ex3.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="v=\sum y_{i}(v)x_{i}=a\sum c_{i}x_{i}\coloneq ae_{1}" display="block"><mrow><mi>v</mi><mo rspace="0.111em">=</mo><mrow><mo movablelimits="false">∑</mo><mrow><msub><mi>y</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>v</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo movablelimits="false">∑</mo><mrow><msub><mi>c</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></mrow><mo>≔</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow></mrow></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.p13" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Note that <math id="Ch3.S2.p13.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\phi(v)=a=\phi(ae_{1})=a\phi(e_{1})" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>ϕ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>v</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mi>a</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>ϕ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mi>ϕ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, so that <math id="Ch3.S2.p13.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\phi(e_{1})=1" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mi>ϕ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></math>.
Thus, <math id="Ch3.S2.p13.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\ker\phi" display="inline"><mrow><mi>ker</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>ϕ</mi></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch3.S2.p13.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\langle e_{1}\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></math> are disjoint.
Moreover, for any <math id="Ch3.S2.p13.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="m" display="inline"><mi>m</mi></math>, then <math id="Ch3.S2.p13.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="m=(m-\phi(m)e_{1})+(\phi(m)e_{1})" display="inline"><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>−</mo><mrow><mi>ϕ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>+</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mrow><mi>ϕ</mi><mo>⁢</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>, so we can write <math id="Ch3.S2.p13.m7" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M=\ker\phi\oplus Re_{1}" display="inline"><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mrow><mi>ker</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>ϕ</mi></mrow><mo>⊕</mo><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.
Similarly, we can write <math id="Ch3.S2.p13.m8" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N=\ker\phi\big{|}_{N}\oplus\langle ae_{1}\rangle" display="inline"><mrow><mi>N</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><msub><mrow><mrow><mi>ker</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>ϕ</mi></mrow><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em" stretchy="true">|</mo></mrow><mi>N</mi></msub><mo>⊕</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟨</mo><mrow><mi>a</mi><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo stretchy="false">⟩</mo></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.
Note that <math id="Ch3.S2.p13.m9" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\dim\ker\phi=m-1" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo rspace="0.167em">dim</mo><mrow><mi>ker</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>ϕ</mi></mrow></mrow><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></mrow></math>.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.p14" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">Finally, we induct to find a basis <math id="Ch3.S2.p14.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left\{{a_{2}e_{2},\ldots,a_{n}e_{n}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><msub><mi>a</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><mrow><msub><mi>a</mi><mi>n</mi></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mi>n</mi></msub></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch3.S2.p14.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left\{{e_{2},\ldots,e_{m}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mo>{</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mi>m</mi></msub><mo>}</mo></mrow></math> of <math id="Ch3.S2.p14.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\ker\phi\big{|}_{N}" display="inline"><msub><mrow><mrow><mi>ker</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>ϕ</mi></mrow><mo maxsize="1.200em" minsize="1.200em" stretchy="true">|</mo></mrow><mi>N</mi></msub></math> and <math id="Ch3.S2.p14.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\ker\phi" display="inline"><mrow><mi>ker</mi><mo lspace="0.167em">⁡</mo><mi>ϕ</mi></mrow></math> repsectively.
Now, <math id="Ch3.S2.p14.m5" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left\{{e_{1},\ldots,e_{m}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mo>{</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mi>m</mi></msub><mo>}</mo></mrow></math> and <math id="Ch3.S2.p14.m6" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left\{{a_{1}e_{1},\ldots,a_{n}e_{n}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mo>{</mo><mrow><msub><mi>a</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><mrow><msub><mi>a</mi><mi>n</mi></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mi>n</mi></msub></mrow><mo>}</mo></mrow></math> wins.
∎</p>
</div>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S2.p15" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">This is a weaker version of the <em class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">incomplete basis theorem</em> for vector spaces, which states that <em class="ltx_emph ltx_font_italic">any</em> basis of <math id="Ch3.S2.p15.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="N" display="inline"><mi>N</mi></math> can be extended to a basis of <math id="Ch3.S2.p15.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M" display="inline"><mi>M</mi></math>.
Moreover, we have to allow additional scaling factors.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section id="Ch3.S3" class="ltx_section">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">3.3 </span>Structure Theorem</h3>

<div id="Ch3.S3.Thmtheorem1" class="ltx_theorem ltx_theorem_theorem">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_title_theorem">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_theorem"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Theorem 3.3.1</span></span><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">.</span>
</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S3.Thmtheorem1.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic">In a PID, <math id="Ch3.S3.Thmtheorem1.p1.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\exists!T,F\triangleleft M" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mrow><mo rspace="0.167em">∃</mo><mo>!</mo></mrow><mo>⁡</mo><mi>T</mi></mrow><mo>,</mo><mrow><mi>F</mi><mo lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em">⊲</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow></math> s.t. <math id="Ch3.S3.Thmtheorem1.p1.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="M=T\oplus F" display="inline"><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo>=</mo><mrow><mi>T</mi><mo>⊕</mo><mi>F</mi></mrow></mrow></math>, where <math id="Ch3.S3.Thmtheorem1.p1.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="T" display="inline"><mi>T</mi></math> torsion and <math id="Ch3.S3.Thmtheorem1.p1.m4" class="ltx_Math" alttext="F" display="inline"><mi>F</mi></math> free.</span></p>
</div>
</div>
<div class="ltx_proof">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_runin ltx_font_italic ltx_title_proof">Proof.</h6>
<div id="Ch3.S3.p1" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p">We prove existence and uniqueness separately.</p>
</div>
<div id="Ch3.S3.p2" class="ltx_para">
<p class="ltx_p"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold">Existence</span>:
Let <math id="Ch3.S3.p2.m1" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\left\{{x_{1},\ldots,x_{m}}\right\}" display="inline"><mrow><mo>{</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>m</mi></msub><mo>}</mo></mrow></math> generating, with <math id="Ch3.S3.p2.m2" class="ltx_Math" alttext="\phi:R^{m}\to M" display="inline"><mrow><mi>ϕ</mi><mo lspace="0.278em" rspace="0.278em">:</mo><mrow><msup><mi>R</mi><mi>m</mi></msup><mo stretchy="false">→</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow></mrow></math> sending <math id="Ch3.S3.p2.m3" class="ltx_Math" alttext="(r_{1},\ldots,r_{m})\mapsto\sum r_{i}x_{i}" display="inline"><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>r</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">…</mi><mo>,</mo><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>m</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo rspace="0.111em" stretchy="false">↦</mo><mrow><mo>∑</mo><mrow><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo>⁢</mo><msub><mi>x</mi><mi>i</mi></msub></mrow></mrow></mrow></math>.
